22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"A mix-and-match vaccine study suggests one shot of AstraZeneca followed by one shot of Pfizer is effective","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/one-shot-covid-vaccine-mix-match-astrazeneca-pfizer-side-effects-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a50409e25d05001880c666?format=jpeg\" alt=\"spain coronavirus\" height=\"1198\" width=\"1598\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Health personnel wear face masks outside the 12 de Octubre Hospital in Madrid, Spain, on March 10, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Pablo Cuadra/Getty Images)</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Giving one shot of AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine and then one dose of Pfizer&#39;s boosted antibodies, study found.</li>\n<li>The side-effects were similar to having two doses of the same vaccine, the scientists said.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Some European countries have stopped using AstraZeneca&#39;s shot in people under 60, after safety concerns.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Vaccinating people with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-vaccine-one-shot-effectiveness-pfizer-moderna-astrazeneca-vaccines-dose-2021-3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one shot of AstraZeneca&#39;s COVID-19</a> vaccine and one shot of Pfizer&#39;s was effective, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-vaccines-compared-vaccine-pfizer-oxford-moderna-astrazeneca-side-effects-2021-2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">side-effects were as expected</a>, researchers from Spain&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.isciii.es/Noticias/Noticias/Paginas/Noticias/Presentaci%c3%b3n-resultados-preliminares-CombivacS.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">leading public health body said Tuesday.</a></p><p>The mix-match study, <a href=\"https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT04860739\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">called CombiVacS</a>, is the first in the world to provide data on the immune response when the vaccine from Pfizer and BioNTech is given after a dose of AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine.</p><p>Antibody levels were about 40 times higher for those who got Pfizer&#39;s vaccine two weeks after AstraZeneca&#39;s, compared with participants who got a single AstraZeneca dose, the researchers from Carlos III Health Institute <a href=\"https://www.isciii.es/Noticias/Noticias/Paginas/Noticias/Presentaci%c3%b3n-resultados-preliminares-CombivacS.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said in a presentation of preliminary results. </a></p><p>The group found that neutralizing antibodies that fight off the virus were boosted more than seven times higher after the dose of Pfizer&#39;s shot. This is higher than described elsewhere with two doses of the same vaccine, they said. </p><p>There were 673 healthy people aged 18 to 60 in the trial, which spanned five different hospitals -  441 people got a dose of AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine followed by a dose of Pfizer&#39;s, while the control group, which didn&#39;t receive a second dose, consisted of 232 people. There was roughly a 50-50 split between the number of women and men in the study. </p><p>The study didn&#39;t directly compare the combination of vaccines with two doses of AstraZeneca&#39;s shot. It&#39;s not clear if the antibody response would be boosted to the same levels when doses were spaced out by more than two weeks.</p><p>The study hasn&#39;t been published as a research paper or scrutinized by other experts in a peer-review. </p><h2><strong>Side effects as expected</strong></h2><p>The Spanish researchers said that side effects after the combination of vaccines lasted about two to three days, and were as expected with two doses of the same shot - but they didn&#39;t directly compare them in the study.</p><p>The most common side effects were injection site discomfort, headache, tiredness, chills, mild nausea, mild cough and fever, they said. The study is not big enough to detect rare adverse events.</p><p>Another <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-vaccine-side-effects-worse-when-mixing-vaccines-study-says-2021-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">mix-match study from Oxford University</a> found that combining Pfizer and AstraZeneca coronavirus vaccines produced worse flu-like side effects than two doses of the same vaccine. The Oxford study researchers are now investigating whether spacing the doses to 12 weeks reduces the side effects.</p><p>Jesus Antonio Frias, clinical director at Carlos III, said that the study&#39;s results supported the possibility of vaccinating patients who have received the first dose from AstraZeneca. But the decision is not up to the study&#39;s investigators, he said.</p><p>Spain stopped using AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine in Spaniards under 60 years-old in April, due to the risk of unusual blood clots. There are about 1.5 million young Spaniards, including health workers, who received one dose of AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine, but have not gotten a second, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/business/healthcare-pharmaceuticals/spain-proposes-pfizer-shots-under-60s-who-got-astrazeneca-first-dose-el-pais-2021-05-18/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to Reuters</a>.</p><p>Other European countries,<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astrazeneca-vaccine-mix-side-effect-blood-clot-covid-2021-4\"> including France and Germany</a>, have already recommended Pfizer&#39;s vaccine as a second dose for those who got AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine as their first.</p><p>But Daniel Lopez Acuna, a former director of the World Health Organization, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/lopezacunad/status/1394628230037053449\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said on Twitter</a> that it was too soon to make public health decisions based on the Spanish study.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/609d65d86a3ce80019e044ff?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"01f020add927ae83b6aec01aec029947","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn32@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-00-756_29a785decca172c4.webp","destWidth":1750,"destHeight":1313,"sourceBytes":286260,"destBytes":286260,"author":"sbaker@businessinsider.com (Sinéad 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"A life coach explains how to strengthen your 'true self' and be more authentic in life and business","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/life-coach-explains-how-to-strengthen-authentic-true-self-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3c3bcf27b4c001944505f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman thinking\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1886\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Being authentic requires letting go of your ego.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/photo/thoughtful-woman-sitting-on-chair-at-home-royalty-free-image/656224595\" target=\"_blank\">Portra/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Life coach Dr. Gurpreet Kaur says it&#39;s important to get in touch with your &#39;true self&#39; to become more authentic.</li>\n<li>An lost sense of self can cause feelings of inadequacy and distraction in your work and personal life.</li>\n<li>Doing at least one thing for yourself daily that makes you feel loved and fulfilled can help restore balance.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The concept of &#34;the true Self&#34; has been present in <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/psychology\">psychology</a>, <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/philosophy\">philosophy</a>, religion, and mysticism for a long <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/time\">time</a>. The current research studies also show a connection between the true Self and the experience of meaning in life, the opposite of despair. </p><h2>Authenticity leads you to your true self</h2><p>Previously, I have talked about the role of ego in <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/article/367568\">feeling fulfilled in life</a>. We explored that there is more than one entity to yourself: the ego and the true Self or the Source or the Spirit/Soul. It doesn&#39;t matter what you call it, but everyone has this pure essence to their being. However, you probably often only identify yourself with the ego, the part of you that is conditioned through fear. The ego keeps you safe, secure, and out of danger. And that is very important for evolutionary purposes. You need to protect yourself.</p><p>When you go up Maslow&#39;s Hierarchy of Needs, you are above and beyond danger. You have reached physical safety so you don&#39;t need the ego as you climb towards the self-actualization state. In fact, you have to drop your ego as you go up the pyramid. You have to be more and more vulnerable by dropping your guards one at a time.</p><p>As you drop these guards, you become more and more authentic and true to yourself first, then to others. This journey through authenticity is what helps you to know your true Self, which I call becoming &#34;God.&#34; Or just when you realize &#34;I am That&#34; as the Vedic expression goes. </p><h2>Your true Self is always connected with the life source that creates everything</h2><p>It is hard to describe and grasp this abstract phenomenon of your true self if you haven&#39;t practiced some sort of <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/mindfulness\">mindfulness</a> witnessing or meditation. In simple language, your true Self is your Spirit or God&#39;s essence within you but it is much more than that. Your true Self is the awareness of the Presence within you that is always and has forever connected with the <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/universe\">Universe</a>. In other words, you are God but feel separated because of the development of the ego.</p><p>As soon as you believe in the truth of the ego, you start to identify yourself with your gender, roles you play, your physical body, your five senses, your abilities, etc. You forget that you are still connected with the life force, the Universe, that creates everything. That&#39;s why it is so much easier for kids to be more creative and imaginative than adults because kids still are and feel connected with the Universe.</p><p>Feeling separated from this life force is what makes you feel inadequate and incomplete because you no longer know or believe in your own greatness. And feeling not loved keeps on adding to the void within you even if you had very loving caregivers. These feelings intensify if you didn&#39;t have loving caregivers or unfortunately experienced trauma(s) or abuse. </p><p>Following is the exercise I highly recommend to practice at least for three weeks to feel the difference: </p><h2>Show up for you</h2><p>Pick one small thing that makes you feel loved. It could be taking a walk, washing your face before bed, taking a long bath, exercise, fully enjoying a cup of coffee, reading a book, etc. Whatever it is, you have to feel loved when you are done with it. If you don&#39;t, try something else next time till you find something that makes you feel loved and fulfilled. You don&#39;t have to take away a ton of time for this exercise. Just put aside about 10 minutes every day to give yourself your unattended attention. </p><p>Do not undermine the power of this simple exercise. When you show up for yourself consistently, you are telling your fragile and afraid ego that you are worthy of this attention, that you matter, and that you are lovable. And this, my friend, is a game-changer. This is exactly what I teach to my clients each step of the way. It&#39;s through baby steps you build the relationship with yourself that helps you connect with your true Self, which is always present. All it requires to present Itself to you is your attention. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Kaur)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60a3c3bcf27b4c001944505f?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn84@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-55-46-205_7d37a72819d99be3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn88@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-05-974_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=EiXrhX2ZB2E:ivWR03Mv9Z8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn56@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-04-119_fc9b58a8fdb877dc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=EiXrhX2ZB2E:ivWR03Mv9Z8:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn4@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-07-408_371a8875239b0d3e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn71@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-33-719_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=EiXrhX2ZB2E:ivWR03Mv9Z8:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn67@2020_5/2021/05/19/14-56-04-188_2c6c59aebeac3d4a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/EiXrhX2ZB2E":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn31@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-01-401_08ddee4074f67e96.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436145867},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"How San Antonio, Texas, is investing in tech, innovation, and infrastructure to become an even greater place to live","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/san-antonio-texas-investing-tech-innovation-infrastructure-2021-5","description":"<div class=\"content-header\"><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/advancing-cities\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603e678a13b221001876b17b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Advancing cities banner v3\" height=\"314\" width=\"2501\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p></div><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60996505ba78eb001906e31b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The University of Texas at San Antonio.\" height=\"1512\" width=\"2016\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University of Texas at San Antonio.\n<p class=\"copyright\">The Office of University Strategic Communications</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>San Antonio expects its population to grow substantially in the next 20 years.</li>\n<li>Its Office of Innovation has a mission to identify community needs and find solutions to do better.</li>\n<li>Current projects include the SmartSA program, the R&#38;D League, and Connected Beyond the Classroom.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\">This article is part of a series focused on American cities building a better tomorrow called &#34;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/advancing-cities\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"5aa3ec3efc15f7a5736de0b51d2ccab0\">Advancing Cities</a>.&#34;</li>\n</ul><p>Over the next 20 years, about <a href=\"https://www.sanantonio.gov/Planning/PlanningUrbanDesign/ComprehensivePlan\">1.1 million more people</a> are expected to call San Antonio, Texas, home, according to <a href=\"https://www.census.gov/newsroom/press-releases/2018/estimates-cities.html\">US Census estimates</a>. To adjust to the influx of new residents and make it an equitable place to live, San Antonio is embracing new technologies and infrastructure.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a280e31b5cea0019c454c0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Griffin.Greg.LowRes\" height=\"289\" width=\"385\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Greg Griffin.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Greg Griffin</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;It&#39;s really about changing the future into something that&#39;s desirable - what we want it to be, as opposed to just following past trends,&#34; <a href=\"http://cacp.utsa.edu/faculty-and-staff/greg-p.-griffin-ph.d\">Greg Griffin</a>, assistant professor of urban and regional planning at the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/university-texas-san-antonio-transportation-problems-tech-traffic-2021-5\">University of Texas at San Antonio</a> (UTSA) College of Architecture, Construction and Planning, told Insider. </p><p>San Antonio&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/san-antonio-texas-office-innovation-smart-tech-infrastructure-divide-2021-5\">Office of Innovation</a> is leading the way in this charge by partnering with UTSA, local utility companies, and other organizations. Chief Innovation Officer <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/brian-dillard-a708093/\">Brian Dillard</a> said the mission is to identify community needs and find solutions.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a281041b5cea0019c454c1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brian Dillard\" height=\"1453\" width=\"1937\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Brian Dillard.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brian Dillard</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;It&#39;s transforming the conversation around innovation from technology-driven to community-driven,&#34; he told Insider. &#34;We&#39;re driven by community demands. We&#39;re driven by doing things in a better way.&#34;</p><p>Here&#39;s a look at some of the projects San Antonio has in the works.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tThe smart-cities program tests projects and tech in a real-world setting\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a27e33f27b4c0019444d2b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Community Solar \" height=\"999\" width=\"1334\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Solar panels in San Antonio.\n<p class=\"copyright\">CPS Energy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The city of San Antonio created the <a href=\"https://www.sanantonio.gov/Innovation/About-Innovation\">Office of Innovation</a> in 2007, originally with the mission to make city services more efficient and effective. About a decade later, the office pivoted its focus and launched smart-cities program <a href=\"https://www.sanantonio.gov/smartsa\">SmartSA</a>.</p><p>Through community partnerships, SmartSA is \"about building a future together,\" Dillard said. \"It's making sure that we're working together rather than apart, as we start to innovate and build these smart-city technologies.\"</p><p>San Antonio designated three areas as \"<a href=\"https://www.sanantonio.gov/Portals/27/Files/SmartSA-Overview.pdf\">innovation zones</a>,\" including downtown, a mixed-use community development in the former Brooks Air Force Base, and the medical center area. There, SmartSA's partners pilot projects and technologies in a real-world setting. So far, projects have focused on addressing the digital divide, sustainability, and mobility in the city.</p>\n\tA new research team will help inform citywide policies\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a27e9ef27b4c0019444d31?format=jpeg\" alt=\"San Antonio\" height=\"1118\" width=\"1491\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>San Antonio traffic.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Eric Gay/ Associated Press</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The Office of Innovation's newest program, the <a href=\"https://www.sanantonio.gov/Innovation/R-D-League#280463953-projects\">R&#38;D League</a>, launched last year. The multidisciplinary research and development team is investigating technology and innovation to create new policies for the city.</p><p>City departments tend to be in \"full execution mode\" and lack the time to devote to research, Dillard said. \"We said, 'Hey, if we're going to do these big changes in city government, we really need to test it out on a smaller scale to identify if it works or not,'\" he added. The research also helps identify what resources are needed to execute the projects.</p><p>Some of the R&#38;D League's projects include creating an ideas portal for the city and adding sensors to solid-waste vehicles and artificial intelligence on traffic cameras. The program works closely with UTSA, USAA, and the Southwest Research Institute.&#160;</p>\n\tAddressing the digital divide has been a priority since before the pandemic\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a27f5e1b5cea0019c454b0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Remote learning\" height=\"2685\" width=\"3580\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>San Antonio students can now access their school district&#39;s network from home.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Marko Geber/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Working with UTSA, the Office of Innovation conducted a digital-divide assessment of residents in 2019 to see who lacked access to broadband internet and where gaps in digital literacy existed. The assessment revealed that about 20% of residents didn't have broadband access.</p><p>\"We didn't want to go down this path of calling ourselves a smart city when a quarter of our residents don't have access to the internet in 2020,\" Dillard said.</p><p>To address the digital divide, the city launched <a href=\"https://covid19.sanantonio.gov/Reports-Statistics/Plans-Reports/Connected-Beyond-the-Classroom\">Connected Beyond the Classroom</a>, an initiative to ensure 20,000 students in San Antonio's most vulnerable neighborhoods can access the internet. The city expanded its existing fiber network into neighborhoods and mounted monopole antennas and small cell towers on schools and libraries to send out a signal. Students were given devices allowing them to log into their school district's network from home.</p><p>Dillard said they're still \"chipping away\" at closing the digital divide in the city, but, \"we do intend to get there.\" The plan is to roll out the program citywide.</p>\n\tA smart-streetlights pilot hopes to identify energy, sustainability, and quality-of-life issues\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a27ccef27b4c0019444d26?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Brooks 4\" height=\"1351\" width=\"1802\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A smart streetlight.\n<p class=\"copyright\">CPS Energy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>San Antonio recently launched a six-month <a href=\"https://newsroom.cpsenergy.com/cps-energy-and-the-city-of-san-antonio-forge-smart-city-agreement-with-att-and-itron/\">Smart Streetlight Technology</a> pilot in partnership with local electric-utility company CPS Energy, AT&#38;T, and Itron. Forty-five existing streetlights in the city's innovation zones were updated so that they can be controlled remotely and outfitted with sensors to test air quality, temperature, ambient noise, parking, and flooding.</p><p>\"At the end of that six months, we'll identify what we think is valuable to our residents and what we think we need to replicate further,\" Dillard said.</p>\n\tThe local electric-utility company aims to update aging infrastructure\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/609bec43342837001822ceaf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Residential Solar 2548 4\" height=\"2756\" width=\"3674\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>CPS Energy installing residential solar panels.\n<p class=\"copyright\">CPS Energy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The winter storm that hit Texas in February 2021 led to massive outages across the state, including in San Antonio, and revealed the fragility of the power grid. CPS Energy, the electric-utility company for San Antonio and the surrounding area, is working on several projects to solve this issue, as well as address sustainability.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.cpsenergy.com/flexiblepath\">Flexible Path</a> is a CPS Energy plan to reduce the use of coal and gas and increase renewable energy usage by 2040. The power company is also working to expand solar and wind power, battery storage, and electric vehicles.</p><p>\"The Flexible Path means not relying on what you've done before,\" CPS Energy President and CEO <a href=\"https://www.cpsenergy.com/en/about-us/who-we-are/senior-leadership.html\">Paula Gold-Williams</a> told Insider. \"Be completely open and find ways to embrace technology and change.\"</p><p>Recently, CPS Energy launched requests for proposal (RFP) to tackle these initiatives. The <a href=\"https://newsroom.cpsenergy.com/cps-energy-launches-community-dialogue-about-its-flexible-path-resource-plan-including-a-focus-on-coal/\">FlexPOWER Bundle</a> will replace aging gas-steam units and increase solar resources, energy storage, and \"all-source firming capacity.\" The <a href=\"https://newsroom.cpsenergy.com/cps-energy-launches-global-rfp-for-next-phase-of-conservation-energy-efficiency-programs-to-help-more-customers/\">FlexSTEP RFP</a> is the next step in the company's Save for Tomorrow Energy Plan (STEP), which emphasizes conservation and energy efficiency.</p><p>CPS Energy plans to announce the projects selected via the RFPs later this year.</p>\n\tA scooter sensor project wants to make the city's transportation more diverse\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a27d2cf27b4c0019444d27?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Scooter 2\" height=\"2455\" width=\"3274\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The ScooterLab project.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Raveen Wijewickrama, PhD student in computer science at UTSA</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>As San Antonio grows, <a href=\"https://spectrumlocalnews.com/tx/san-antonio/traffic/2019/06/11/could-san-antonio-s-traffic-congestion-cripple-the-city--\">traffic</a> is becoming a problem. Researchers at UTSA are examining ways to make the city more bike-, pedestrian-, and scooter-friendly.</p><p>One of the university's projects is <a href=\"https://scooterlab.utsa.edu/\">ScooterLab</a>. Through this initiative, electronic scooters and other micromobility devices will be outfitted with sensors to better understand how residents use them and any safety issues.</p><p>\"We're trying to develop what we call a micromobility test bed to be able to support all those different types of studies,\" Griffin said. \"We can potentially test different scenarios that make mobility solutions more equitable and efficient.\"&#160;</p><p>The data collected will inform infrastructure development to better accommodate different modes of transportation in the city, he said. ScooterLab, which is in the early stages, recently received a National Science Foundation grant.</p>\n\tCrowdsourcing bike traffic data will make roads safer\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a27fbd1b5cea0019c454b3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Strava\" height=\"1331\" width=\"1780\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Strava app.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/ron-alford-shows-his-bike-app-called-strava-that-allows-news-photo/159560490?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Tracy A. Woodward/The Washington Post via Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Building better bike infrastructure in San Antonio starts with knowing where residents and visitors are cycling, Griffin said. \"We're working toward solving the problem of being able to identify where real safety problems are,\" he added.</p><p>Part of Griffin's research involves <a href=\"https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/0361198120946016\">crowdsourcing bicycle traffic volumes</a>, using apps like Strava and other methods, and he's published several studies on the subject. This uncovers where bike-related accidents are occurring and where bike traffic is increasing and decreasing.</p><p>The research could help the city know which intersections may need to be reconfigured or roadways need bike lanes to adapt to bike traffic.</p>\n\tEngaging and informing the community is central to the city's mission\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a2800bf27b4c0019444d39?format=jpeg\" alt=\"San Antonio, Texas\" height=\"4320\" width=\"5760\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>San Antonio, Texas.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Engaging the community is a central part of the Office of Innovation's work. Before the pandemic, they launched the<a href=\"https://www.sanantonio.gov/gpa/News/ArtMID/24373/ArticleID/18104/%E2%80%9CSmartSA-Sandbox%E2%80%9D-Comes-to-Brooks-Innovation-Zone\"> SmartSA Sandbox</a>, which are events showcasing smart technology, such as smart sensors and autonomous vehicles, and giving residents the chance to test it out, Dillard said. The events have been on hold for the past year, but the office plans to restart the SmartSA Sandbox soon.</p><p>The city has also placed <a href=\"https://www.viainfo.net/2019/07/08/via-launches-its-first-ike-smart-city-kiosk-at-centro-plaza/\">interactive digital kiosks</a> around the city. Residents can use the kiosks to access directions, traffic information, and information about city services. They also serve as free WiFi hotspots.</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a excerpt of The Atlantic&#39;s Edward-Isaac Dovere&#39;s forthcoming book, titled &#34;Battle for the Soul.&#34;</p><p>&#34;With what he cares about, what he fights for, what he&#39;s committed to, you day masks came off. Here&#39;s what a &#39;hard pass&#39; and fewer restrictions mean for us - and our reporting.</a></em></p><p>Harris and her team decided to land a strategic punch on Biden in the debate to boost her fundraising and standing in the polls as 2019&#39;s second fundraising quarter drew to a close. </p><p>At that point in the race, Biden <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/25/us/joe-biden-crime-laws.html\">was facing scrutiny over his long and complicated record</a> on racial justice issues including school busing and criminal justice - a news cycle partly driven by the opposition research work of Harris&#39; team, according to Dovere&#39;s book. </p><p>Right before the debate, Biden garnered controversy for comments he made at a New York City fundraiser <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-democrats-joe-bidens-record-before-debates-2019-6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"853539306304cdc2a63542ddfe5d6f48\">fondly remembering the days of &#34;civility&#34; in the Senate</a> when he worked with people he didn&#39;t agree with, including two Democratic senators who supported segregation.</p><p>&#34;I was in a caucus with James O. Eastland. He never called me &#39;boy,&#39; he always called me &#39;son,&#39;&#34; Biden said. &#34;Well guess what? At least there was some civility. We got things done. We didn&#39;t agree on much of anything. We got things done. We got it finished.&#34;</p><p>Harris, who is biracial, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/kamala-spars-with-biden-calls-comments-race-personal-and-hurtful-2019-6\">confronted Biden at the debate, saying</a>, &#34;I do not believe you are a racist and I agree with you when you commit yourself to the importance of finding common ground, but it&#39;s personal and it was hurtful to hear you talk about the reputations of two United States Senators who built their reputations and career on the segregation of race in this country.&#34;</p><p>Harris then hit Biden over his controversial record on school busing.</p><p>&#34;There was a little girl in California who was part of the second class to integrate her public schools and she was bused to school every day,&#34; she said. &#34;That little girl was me. So I will tell you that on this subject, it cannot be an intellectual debate among Democrats.&#34;</p><p>Biden responded: &#34;It&#39;s a mischaracterization of my position across the board. I do not praise racists. That is not true.&#34; He also cited his time working as a public defender for the cause of civil rights before becoming a senator. </p><p>After the debate ended, Biden leaned to his right and said, &#34;Well, that was some f---ing bullshit&#34; to fellow 2020 candidate and now-Secretary of Transportation Pete Buttigieg, Dovere wrote. </p><p>Dovere&#39;s book, &#34;<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Battle-Soul-Inside-Democrats-Campaigns/dp/1984878077\">Battle for the Soul: Inside the Democrats&#39; Campaigns to Defeat Trump</a><em>,&#34;</em> which gives an inside It could provide clues to officials&#39; views on the economic recovery and further details on how they define &#34;transitory&#34; inflation. </p><p>&#34;Growth remains robust and there has been no material change to the bullish narrative,&#34; said Craig Johnson, Piper Sandler&#39;s chief market technician. &#34;We suspect economic uncertainty and volatility could remain high over the coming months and temporary pull the bulls&#39; foot off the gas as they wait for validation of the Fed&#39;s transitory inflation forecast.&#34; </p><p><strong>Here&#39;s where US indexes stood shortly billionaire as the founder of the &#39;Robinhood of India.&#39; He told us why millennials and Gen Zers have an investing edge over their predecessors and shared his advice for retail be paid in<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/ransomware-cryber-attack-bitcoin-btc-cryptocurrency-regulation-sec-2021-5-1030445784\">cryptocurrencies have also added to class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>JPMorgan, headed up by CEO Jamie Dimon, is the biggest US bank by assets. </li>\n<li>JPMorgan this week shook up leadership of its massive consumer bank. </li>\n<li>JPMorgan has also made new digital banking hires, including poaching an exec from Goldman. </li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider&#39;s homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>JPMorgan is the biggest bank in the US and a bellwether for the global financial system. So when the firm&#39;s senior-most leaders talk, Wall Street pays attention.</p><p>The bank on May 18 promoted two women to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-lake-piepszak-community-bank-gordon-smith-dimon-succession-2021-5\">co-lead the firm&#39;s massive consumer and community banking business</a>: consumer-lending chief Marianne Lake and chief financial officer Jennifer Piepszak. The pair will take over running the division from Gordon Smith, who made the surprising announcement that he was retiring this year from his roles as co-president and co-chief operating officer of the firm and CEO of CCB. </p><p>The moves shine a light on succession planning at the firm, as Lake and Piepszak are two of the top contenders to take over for CEO Jamie Dimon when he eventually retires. Smith had also been rumored to be in the running for the top job before announcing his retirement.</p><p>JPMorgan also continues to feast on hires from Goldman Sachs&#39; Marcus division: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/wall-street-hires-and-exits-jpmorgan-barclays-blackrock-deutsche-bank-2021-5?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sherry Ann Mohan</a>, a 15-year Goldman veteran who was mostly recently CFO of the bank&#39;s consumer business, will start as CFO of JPMorgan&#39;s business banking in August. This comes after the bank <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-chase-key-hires-bolster-digital-banking-team-sonali-divilek-2021-4?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">poached three Marcus</a> executives in April. </p><p>JPMorgan is also beefing up its tech offerings for employees, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-cio-chief-information-officers-promotion-tech-innovation-employee-experience-2021-5?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">appointing CIOs</a> to newly formed groups.</p><p>The bank <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-return-to-office-plans-may-july-rotation-memo-reopening-2021-4?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">opened its U.S. offices on May 17 and is requiring all employees to come in by July</a>, according to an internal memo sent in May. JPMorgan is also planning to bring <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-chase-internships-investment-bank-markets-office-summer-jamie-dimon-2021-4?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"13a3367fa495023af737933844bad9bd\">some interns to the office this summer,</a> and CEO Jamie Dimon has said he expects staff to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgans-ceo-jamie-dimon-return-to-office-instagram-face-masks-2021-4?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">maskless in the office</a> later this year.</p><p><strong>Read more: </strong></p><ul><li><em><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-lake-piepszak-community-bank-gordon-smith-dimon-succession-2021-5?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">JPMorgan just named 2 new co-heads of consumer banking, and the leadership shakeup gives clues to who will eventually take over from CEO Jamie Dimon</a></em></li><li><em><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-return-to-office-plans-may-july-rotation-memo-reopening-2021-4?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">JPMorgan just told US workers it wants them coming into the office on a &#39;consistent rotational schedule&#39; by early July</a></em></li></ul><section><section><section></section></section></section><h2>Recent hires and exits at JPMorgan</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6095669534af8d001859c09a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"collage (1)\" height=\"3000\" width=\"4000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Melissa Goldman and James Reid\n<p class=\"copyright\">JPMorgan</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>There have been many opportunities in recent weeks for existing JPMorgan executives to step into new roles at the firm. In addition to Marianne Lake&#39;s and  Jennifer Piepszak&#39;s promotions to co-heads of consumer and community banking, the firm named James Reid and Melissa Goldman to be CIOs of two newly-formed groups to help modernize tech for employees.</p><p>Reid is CIO of the firm&#39;s employee experience and corporate technology organization, which is modernizing the tech employees use internally. And Goldman, also the firm&#39;s chief data officer, is CIO of the finance, risk, data, and controls (FRDC) technology group.</p><p>JPMorgan also hired another ex-Marcus executive, Sherry Ann Mohan, chief financial officer for business banking, <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/05/14/goldman-sachs-loses-cfo-of-marcus-business-to-jpmorgan-chase.html\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"a25f7298ddbf61a1b9f75826605a5193\">CNBC first reported</a>. Mohan, who will start August, was previously at Goldman Sachs for 15 years and most recently the CFO of the consumer business, including the Marcus brand and Apple Card.</p><p>And the bank&#39;s former global head of diversity and inclusion for the wealth and asset management business, Tia Counts, departed last week for index giant MSCI, where she will be the new chief diversity and inclusion officer.</p><p><strong>More on people moves here:</strong></p><ul><li><em><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-cio-chief-information-officers-promotion-tech-innovation-employee-experience-2021-5?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">JPMorgan just named 2 CIOs to newly formed groups focused on improving employees&#39; experience using the bank&#39;s tech</a></em></li><li><em><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-chase-key-hires-bolster-digital-banking-team-sonali-divilek-2021-4?r=jpm-lp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">JPMorgan Chase poached a top Marcus exec along with key hires from Wells Fargo and Google to support a &#39;huge agenda&#39; for digital banking</a></em></li></ul><h2>Wealth management plans</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6002f123660f6c0018349951?format=jpeg\" alt=\"MASPETH, NY - NOVEMBER 17: Shivani Siroya, Kristin Lemkau and Stephanie Cohen speak onstage at Girlboss Rally NYC 2018 at Knockdown Center on November 17, 2018 in Maspeth, New York. Over the next five to six years, the bank is considering hiring as many as 4,000 advisors to roughly double its current base, US Wealth Management Chief Executive Officer <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-wealth-management-financial-advisor-recruitment-plans-kristin-lemkau-hires-2020-10?r=jpm-lp\">Kristin Lemkau</a> told Business Insider this fall. </p><p>Lemkau, who has been with the bank for over two decades and was previously <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-chase-has-named-leslie-gillin-as-its-new-cmo-2020-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"e2bec0b81bd8daf0efea345a99f07148\">its chief marketing officer</a>, was named head of JPMorgan&#39;s new wealth division in December 2019. href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=inges Bell</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>The cryptocurrency market has been having a rough few days, causing a key investor sentiment metric to fall to lows not seen since April 2020.</p><p>The &#34;<a href=\"https://alternative.me/crypto/fear-and-greed-index/\">crypto fear and greed index</a>,&#34; published by Alternative.me, fell to 23 on Wednesday from a high of 75 last week, indicating a substantial fall to &#34;Extreme Fear&#34; from &#34;Extreme Greed.&#34;</p><p>This level implies investors are feeling worried to the point that they are more likely to retreat from the crypto market. That could push prices even lower, creating a good buying opportunity for those looking to enter. Conversely, a feeling of extreme greed suggests assets may be overvalued, and a downward correction is due.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a50f1ff27b4c0019445458?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Screenshot 2021 05 19 at 14.13.27\" height=\"656\" width=\"722\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alternative.me</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><em><strong>Read More:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/millennial-investing-tips-outlook-robinhood-of-india-founder-nikhil-kamath-2021-5\" data-analytics-position=\"5\" data-analytics-module=\"\">Nikhil Kamath became a 34-year-old billionaire as the founder of the &#39;Robinhood of India.&#39; He told us why millennials and Gen Zers have an investing edge over their predecessors and shared his advice for retail traders.</a></em></p><p>The last time the index flashed a level between 20-23 was in April 2020, when pandemic-driven volatility had just hit global markets.</p><p>&#34;An extremely fearful market like this has historically presented solid buying opportunities during bull cycles,&#34; researchers at Norway-based Arcane said in a <a href=\"https://www.research.arcane.no/blog/week19\">Tuesday report</a>.</p><p>Another closely-tracked cryptocurrency ratio called the &#34;Grayscale discount&#34; is reflecting that investors are definitely nervous, according to the analysis firm.</p><p>That discount, which marks the difference between the price of bitcoin and the spot trading price, has widened to a record 25%. &#34;If the discount becomes of sufficient size, this could post a short-term risk for bitcoin,&#34; Arcane wrote.</p><p>Furthermore, bitcoin&#39;s volatility in the short-term exhibits notable fluctuations over the past month. The current level of volatility over the past 30 days shows that its price has moved 4.5% each day, according to the <a href=\"https://www.buybitcoinworldwide.com/volatility-index/\">Bitcoin Volatility Index</a>.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-cryptocurrencies-china-crypto-crackdown-price-outlook-2021-5-1030445035\">Bitcoin plunged</a> as much as 26% to below $33,000 on Wednesday after China said virtual currencies cannot and should not be used in the market as they don&#39;t have real value. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/doge-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dogecoin</a> fell 43% to 28 cents and Ethereum&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/eth-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">ether</a> fell 39% to $2,094.</p><p>The broad weakness across cryptocurrencies came from the next step in Beijing&#39;s regulatory crackdown, according to Edward Moya, a senior market analyst at OANDA. &#34;China&#39;s restrictions on cryptocurrencies are expanding and that has many investors nervous that panic-selling will continue,&#34; he said.</p><p>The crash in the cryptocurrency market has a lot of the new institutional money see all their profits go up in smoke, he said, adding a panic-selling event will prompt investors to be selective and buy the coins they think will survive more intense regulation.</p><div up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Institutional investors are switching out of bitcoin and are instead returning to gold, for the first time in six months, JPMorgan research analysts said in a note on Tuesday. </p><p>A combination of rising inflation, tightening regulation and ripples running through the online crypto community after Elon Musk announced that Tesla would no longer be accepting bitcoin as a form of payment for environmental reasons have caused bitcoin&#39;s price to tumble in recent weeks. </p><p>Since hitting a record high of almost $65,000 in mid-April the asset has lost around half its value to last trade around $35,470 on Wednesday.</p><p>&#34;The bitcoin flow picture continues to deteriorate and is pointing to continued retrenchment by institutional investors. Over the past month, bitcoin futures markets experienced their steepest and more sustained liquidation since the bitcoin ascent started last October,&#34; JPMorgan said. </p><p>Momentum traders including crypto funds that have unwound assets recently are partially responsible for this, according to the research note. A key momentum indicator has therefore turned negative from a short term perspective, which could lead to more traders selling off their assets. </p><p>In the longer term however, the momentum indicator is still positive. &#34;It is perhaps too early to characterize bitcoin as oversold,&#34; JPMorgan said, adding that bitcoin futures and related products had also been affected by the drop in value of the digital asset.</p><p>&#34;What is striking is that the recent outflows from bitcoin funds have been accompanied by inflows into gold ETFs in a reversal of the last quarter of 2020 and the beginning of this year,&#34; the research note said, adding that a similar pattern can be observed with futures contracts on the two assets. </p><p>Large parts of the crypto community have hailed bitcoin as the new gold, especially young investors who see it as a more worthwhile investment compared to bullion, which has earned bitcoin the nickname &#34;millennial gold&#34;. </p><p>The ongoing shift is mostly driven by institutional investors, JPMorgan said. From an institutional perspective, flows into bitcoin began to slow down during the first three months of this year and turned negative at the beginning of the second quarter. In comparison, retail flows have stayed relatively stable throughout. </p><p>The reasons behind the shift are however unclear, although JPMorgan said bitcoin&#39;s volatility, especially the speed at which it tends to fall, was at odds with gold&#39;s greater price stability. </p><p>&#34;Or they perhaps view the current bitcoin price as too high relative to gold and thus do the opposite of what they did in the previous two quarters, i.e. they sell bitcoin and buy gold,&#34; the bank said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"I recruit nannies, personal chefs, and even palace managers for the ultra-wealthy. Here's what it's like to deal with the 1% every single day.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/job-diary-recruit-household-staff-for-uhnwi-ultra-wealthy-homes-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3c1d2f27b4c0019445054?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Darren Lewis\" height=\"2158\" width=\"2877\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Darren Lewis.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Darren Lewis</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>Darren Lewis is an executive staff recruiter based in London, England.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>He recruits nannies, personal chefs, and chiefs of staff to run the homes of wealthy clients, including celebs and athletes, around the world.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>This is what his job is like, as told to freelance writer Chrissie McClatchie.</strong></li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>We&#39;ve all spent a lot of time at home during the pandemic, even the richest people in the world. As a result, there&#39;s never been more demand for highly qualified household staff. As the cofounder and director of Pembury Partners Household Consultancy (Pembury), I&#39;m the person some of the world&#39;s wealthiest have on speed dial when they&#39;re looking to hire executive staff for their private residence - or residences.</p><p>I wasn&#39;t looking to start my own business. For the last few years, I&#39;ve been at a senior level within the private household recruiting sector. When the pandemic first hit, my team and I were put on furlough, and that became the catalyst I needed. I gave Evie Dakin, a colleague and good friend of mine, a call and told her we should go it alone. It was hard to take that first step, but we haven&#39;t looked back since.</p><p>Pembury officially became operational in June 2020. Our offices are in London&#39;s Mayfair neighborhood, although I&#39;ve been working at home for the better part of the year. For the first six months it was just Evie and I doing everything from business development to accounts and marketing. At the end of last year we made our first hires, a project manager and expert in childcare recruitment. </p><h2><strong>Currently, we&#39;re working with about 100 UHWNI clients, many of whom are celebrities and athletes.</strong></h2><p>Dealing with the 1% everyday is super intense, especially because all of my clients want to have hired someone yesterday. But that&#39;s nothing different to recruiting for the luxury hotel space, where I&#39;ve also worked before. The UHNWIs (ultra-high-net-worth individuals) of the world want their home to be run like a six-star hotel, too.</p><p>At any one time, we could be looking to fill any range of roles in a number of locations. For example, we&#39;re currently recruiting for a property and assets manager in Azerbaijan, a chief of staff in London, and a palace manager in Qatar. </p><p>For many people, the past 12 months have been tough for business but for us it&#39;s been nothing short of a boon. We&#39;ve really pushed through COVID and are growing all the time. </p><h2><strong>We staff for all types of specialty positions, such as performance chefs for professional footballers. </strong></h2><p>By performance chefs, I mean people that cook the right meals for sportsmen and women, chefs that have formal education in nutritional science and who know what are the key ingredients for optimal athletic performance. It&#39;s definitely a growing trend that we&#39;re also seeing cross over into the UHNWI space - healthy living is the phrase on everyone&#39;s lips right now.</p><p>It&#39;s quite a niche market, but once one professional athlete hires a chef, they all want a chef. It&#39;s something we&#39;ve never done before but it&#39;s been hugely successful so far.</p><p>We don&#39;t employ staff on behalf of our clients, we&#39;re just an introducer and charge our clients a percentage of the candidate&#39;s first year salary as a fee. Right now, that&#39;s 25%.</p><p>In terms of salary range, nannies can expect to earn between $55,000 to $140,000 depending on experience, chefs between $70,000 and $350,000, and chief of staffs from $100,000 to $425,000.</p><p>Although some candidates register with us in response to vacancies listed on our website or on social media platforms like Linkedin, we mostly head hunt. While travel restrictions and local quarantines have been obstacles to navigate, Evie and I have the right knowledge and know the right tools to be able to track down the right pool of candidates anywhere in the world.</p><h2><strong>Most people we hire must have prior experience in private households, or on superyachts or in luxury chalets.</strong></h2><p>A stable CV is essential, as is five years of excellent references and a clean criminal record. The vetting process is extensive and to the highest standards. Once we put a candidate forward, they then connect with the principal client or their representative for a face-to-face or video interview.</p><p>After filling a vacancy, we don&#39;t follow up with performance reviews, but I did place a chef in a training camp for a World Champion Boxer who retained his title with one of his best performances, so I like to think that had something to do with it. Feedback is always welcome, although unusual. </p><p>This week I had a chef on trial with a British billionaire and the female principal client texted me after the meal to say she loved them. That was nice. Because we reference check every candidate we put forward, and they trial with the client, it&#39;s rare that anyone is ever unhappy once a placement has been made.</p><h2><strong>We may get a call at 5 p.m. on a Friday afternoon asking for someone by Monday morning. </strong></h2><p>Evie and I don&#39;t work fixed hours, as is usual in the UHNWI space. If I&#39;m working for clients on the west coast of the US, I&#39;ll adjust my hours to be on their time for as long as required.</p><p>There is one rule I abide by as much as possible, however, and that is to not work on a Saturday. I&#39;m Jewish and practicing so I keep from sundown Friday to sundown Saturday as my protected family time. For the other six days, there&#39;s no holds barred, and I&#39;ll pick up my phone 24/7.</p><p>It may sound draining but my job does allow me to work from anywhere in the world and be with my family. In August we will visit Israel for the month. I&#39;ll work early before my children wake up, and then we can spend the morning together, probably at the beach. I&#39;ll work for a couple of hours when it&#39;s really hot in the afternoon and then we can go out at night. At home back in London, I usually break up the day with time on my Peloton.</p><h2><strong>I deal with household names daily, so the expectations are high (and some egos are extremely big).</strong></h2><p>It&#39;s fascinating working with UHNWI and celebrity names, but in the end it becomes normal and it&#39;s not really something I talk too much about with my social circle. Of course, NDA&#39;s prohibit me from sharing too much detail, but, in any case, many of my friends wouldn&#39;t understand the world I live in and the inner lifestyle of UHNWIs.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3c25ff27b4c0019445055?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Darren Lewis\" height=\"934\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A course by the private chef for Lewis&#39; at-home anniversary dinner.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Darren Lewis</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>My wife and I recently celebrated our 10-year wedding anniversary during Britain&#39;s COVID-19 lockdown. Since we couldn&#39;t go out to mark the occasion, I asked one of the best private chefs around to come and cook our anniversary meal. Vegan cuisine is his speciality, and he&#39;s previously worked for Claudia Schiffer and Stella McCartney. </p><p>Later this month it&#39;s my birthday and weather permitting, I&#39;m hosting six friends in my garden and will have a private chef come and cater our meal. I guess you could say those are definitely the &#34;perks&#34; of the job.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a vaccine&#39;s antibodies were &#34;a little bit weaker against the variants, but not enough that we think it would have much of an effect on the protective ability of the vaccines,&#34; senior author Nathaniel Landau <a href=\"https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210517-pfizer-moderna-vaccines-effective-against-indian-variants-study\">told AFP on Monday</a>.</p><p>There is &#34;no reason to B.1.427/B.1.429, first identified in California, and the B.1.1.7 variant first seen in the UK, Fauci said on Tuesday. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Guenot)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60a4d1f6f27b4c00194453e2?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn48@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-05-740_3b3788cac8c255f2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn88@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-05-974_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=e6yEurxJ58k:9G_K-29fCBs:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn44@2020_5/2021/05/19/14-56-02-476_0a3352f7ea8f56aa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=e6yEurxJ58k:9G_K-29fCBs:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn48@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-03-457_146ac18a189f4c3e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn71@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-33-719_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=e6yEurxJ58k:9G_K-29fCBs:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn31@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-07-055_3a5ffb18c3b85ac1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/e6yEurxJ58k":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn16@2020_5/2021/05/19/14-56-07-558_ff867118d7568fa1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436145873},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"Immigrants who have been in the US for decades are being tossed into courtrooms without lawyers because of a glaring loophole in our justice system - it's time they get a fair hearing","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/immigrants-facing-deportation-trials-without-legal-representation-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/609ede3a1b5cea0019c45294?format=jpeg\" alt=\"People holding a banner that reads &#34;Protect Immigrants and End Deportation&#34;\" height=\"4023\" width=\"5365\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>United We Dream, CASA, and other organizations celebrate passage of the American Dream and Promise Act (HR 6) in the House during their watch part and rally on the National Mall in Washington on Thursday, March 18, 2021\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bill Clark/CQ-Roll Call, Inc/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The majority of immigrants facing deportation lack an attorney because they are only charged with a civil violation. </li>\n<li>Federal, state, and local leadership can protect immigrants by advancing universal representation to immigrants who cannot otherwise afford it.</li>\n<li>Annie Chen is the director of the Vera Institute of Justice&#39;s SAFE Initiative, which partners with local governments, lawyers, and advocates to secure legal defense programs for people facing detention and deportation.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The first 100 days of the Biden Administration have seen record numbers of immigrants <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/immigration/border-apprehensions-rose-slightly-april-number-unaccompanied-minors-dropped-n1267046\">arriving</a> at the US-Mexico border, with Border Patrol encountering almost 180,000 immigrants in the month of April alone - a 15-year high. But with the focus on the crisis at the border, we&#39;ve overlooked the ongoing immigration crisis in our backyards. Community members are still facing detention and are at risk of deportation and permanent separation from their families as a result of years of anti-immigrant federal policies - including Marco Munoz Quiroz, who has lived in the US for decades, and whose entire family are US citizens.</p><p>Quiroz could not afford an attorney after he was arrested at his home in Southern California in January. If he had been facing criminal charges, the government would have provided a public defender to protect his rights. But because he stood accused of civil immigration violations, he was not guaranteed legal defense. He spent more than a month fearing deportation and worrying about his health at the Otay Mesa Detention Center, a facility he described as unbearably cold.</p><p>While the Biden Administration has taken some initial steps toward reversing the aggressively anti-immigrant agenda of the prior administration, Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) and federal immigration authorities have <a href=\"https://theintercept.com/2021/05/07/ice-biden-priorities-deportation/\">continued</a> to target immigrant communities, book people into detention, and tear apart families. Even after the Biden Administration <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/2021/2/19/22290118/biden-ice-immigration-enforcement-memo\">made</a> changes to ICE enforcement policies, Quiroz and others with long histories of peaceful life in America are still being ensnared.</p><p>As a result, some immigrants <a href=\"https://immigrationforum.org/article/supreme-court-ruling-made-indefinite-immigrant-detention-the-law-of-the-land/\">endure</a> detention for weeks, months, or even years, often under inhumane and <a href=\"https://www.vera.org/tracking-covid-19-in-immigration-detention\">deadly</a> conditions that have been exacerbated by the pandemic. As of May 2021, ICE confirmed that more than 14,000 people had tested positive for COVID-19 at 133 different facilities, and the Vera Institute of Justice&#39;s research demonstrates that the actual number of infections in ICE detention is far higher.</p><p>The majority of immigrants facing deportation, including <a href=\"https://www.vera.org/downloads/publications/support-universal-representation-safe-network-101.pdf\">70%</a> of those in detention, lack an attorney, leaving them to navigate a complex and unjust system without legal defense.</p><p>Fortunately, Quiroz lives in one of a growing number of places where state and local governments have set up public defender-style systems to ensure that no one faces deportation without a lawyer simply because they cannot afford one. As a result, an experienced removal defense immigration attorney from the Oakland-based nonprofit Immigrant Legal Defense (ILD) provided Quiroz with legal representation. ILD also partnered with the California Collaborative for Immigrant Justice on a public campaign resulting in daily phone calls to ICE and immigration authorities from Quiroz&#39;s family, community members, and immigrant rights supporters demanding Quiroz be released from detention. More than one month later, ICE released Quiroz home to his family. Since then, the immigration judge terminated Quiroz&#39;s deportation proceedings and he is no longer at risk of being deported.</p><h2><strong>Immigrants need guaranteed legal defense</strong></h2><p>We need action at all levels of government. The Biden administration can build a <a href=\"https://www.vera.org/publications/a-federal-defender-service-for-immigrants\">federally-funded, universal legal defense service</a> that provides representation to all immigrants. But state and local leadership is key and must continue to step up to protect immigrants in our communities by supporting public defender-style deportation defense systems that provide high quality legal defense to immigrants like Quiroz who cannot otherwise afford it.</p><p>Amid the pandemic, lawyers and legal service providers in deportation defense programs across the country remain on the front lines fighting every day for their clients, and it is making a difference. Immigrants who are <a href=\"https://www.vera.org/blog/immigrants-facing-deportation-do-not-have-the-right-to-a-publicly-funded-attorney-heres-how-to-change-that\">represented</a> are three and a half times more likely to be released from detention on bond and up to 10 times more likely to establish a right to remain in the United States. </p><p>Deportation defense programs are also a common-sense policy solution widely supported by the public, across political lines. <a href=\"https://www.vera.org/downloads/publications/taking-the-pulse-national-polling-v2.pdf\">Polling</a> by the Vera Institute of Justice has shown that two in three people in the United States, or 67%, support government-funded attorneys for immigrants facing deportation. Although legal defense alone cannot undo the decades of systemic issues facing immigrants, it is a necessary check on the unjust system of criminalization and mass detention of immigrants that particularly targets over-policed immigrants of color.</p><p>As communities seek to invest in programs with a community-driven vision of public safety and justice, more than 40 cities, counties, and states have continued, expanded, and created new deportation defense programs. <a href=\"https://www.houstonchronicle.com/news/houston-texas/houston/article/Harris-County-OKs-2-5M-to-help-poor-immigrants-15717330.php\">Harris County, Texas</a>, <a href=\"https://denverite.com/2021/03/24/denvers-immigrant-legal-defense-fund-got-a-big-boost-this-week/\">Denver</a>, <a href=\"https://justicecorps.org/news/prince-georges-county-pledges-half-a-million-dollars-towards-access-to-counsel-for-detained-immigrants/\">Prince George&#39;s County, Maryland</a>, and the state of <a href=\"https://www.afsc.org/resource/nj-coalition-immigrant-representation-applauds-increased-funding-to-detention-and\">New Jersey</a> have dedicated increased funding for deportation defense programs, while the states of <a href=\"https://www.wbez.org/stories/illinois-lawmakers-want-to-explore-providing-legal-help-to-immigrants-facing-deportation/56d5aeba-d1ca-40d5-ae78-3358efbba0dd\">Illinois</a> and <a href=\"https://www.coloradopolitics.com/opinion/immigrants-as-well-have-a-right-to-an-attorney/article_5555de6e-9b43-11eb-9e42-5b90235572c2.html\">Colorado</a> consider similar efforts. A promising new program was recently approved in <a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/california-border-county-votes-fund-legal-aid-migrants-facing-deportation-1589023\">San Diego County, California</a> that makes legal defense at the Otay Mesa Detention Center, where Quiroz was detained, a reality for more people who desperately need it.</p><p>Local and state policies that ensure due process and repair the most broken aspects of our immigration system have charted a path forward for federal action. And this critical work must continue across all levels of government. Local and state leaders, community organizations, and legal service providers can hasten progress towards a more just system by joining the movement to secure, protect, and champion counsel for people facing deportation. All of us deserve a right to due process when our life, liberty, or community ties are at stake.</p><p><em>Annie Chen is the director of the Vera Institute of Justice&#39;s SAFE Initiative, which partners with local and state governments, lawyers, and advocates to secure legal defense programs for people facing detention and deportation.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original 12.</li>\n<li><strong><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=inges target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Cryptocurrency linked-stocks plummeted on Wednesday amid massive sell-offs in crypto leaders <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd\">bitcoin</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/eth-usd\">ethereum</a>.</p><p>Shares of the cryptocurrency exchange, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/coin-stock\">Coinbase</a>, fell as much as 10%, while shares of cryptocurrency miners like <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/riot-stock\">Riot Blockchain</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/mara-stock\">Marathon Digital Holdings</a> were down as much as 17% and 18%, respectively.</p><p>Michael Saylor&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/mstr-stock\">Microstrategy</a>, which just &#34;<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/microstrategy-buys-the-dip-%E2%80%94-now-has-more-btc-than-us-govt-9635350\">bought the dip</a>&#34; in bitcoin with $10 million at an average price of $43,663 per coin, was down as much as 15% on the day.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/etfs/grayscale-bitcoin-trust-btc-us3896371099\">Grayscale Bitcoin Trust</a> sank more than 12% on Wednesday as well, and even Tesla saw its stock drop more than 4% on the dark day for cryptocurrency enthusiasts. </p><p>Cryptocurrencies as a whole saw roughly 24% wiped off their total market cap on the day, according to data from <a href=\"https://coinmarketcap.com/\">CoinMarketCap.com</a>, as altcoins fell in tandem with crypto leaders bitcoin and ethereum.</p><p>All of the top ten cryptocurrencies by market cap, except the stablecoin <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/usdt-usd\">Tether</a>, fell double digits on Wednesday.</p><p>The cryptocurrency bear market began on May 12, when Elon Musk tweeted that Tesla would <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-bans-bitcoin-payments-due-to-impact-on-environment-2021-5?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest&r=US&IR=T=US&#38;IR=T\">no longer accept bitcoin</a> as a payment method due to the environmental impact of its computational mining tactic for minting new coins.</p><p>Then on Tuesday, the Chinese government <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-rally-china-bans-banks-crypto-business-btc-2021-5-1030442848\">reinforced its previous ban</a> on financial institutions and payments companies operating in the cryptocurrency business.</p><p>The National Internet Finance Association of China, the China Banking Association, and the Payment and Clearing Association of China said in a statement that cryptocurrencies &#34;are not supported by real value&#34; and argued speculative trading of cryptocurrencies is &#34;seriously infringing on the safety of people&#39;s property and disrupting the normal economic and financial order.&#34;</p><p>The historic single-day fall for cryptocurrencies comes just a day after <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/brphf-stock\">Galaxy Digital&#39;s</a> Mike Novogratz shrugged off the recent crypto-slump.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s easy to get buried in the volatility of the day,&#34; Novogratz said, according to a transcript on Sentieo, a financial-research site. &#34;Elon Musk&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/elon-musk-tesla-bitcoin-adoption-halted-climate-criticisms-2021-5-1030432474?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter comments</a>, bitcoin going down 4,000 points, and everyone starts running around like chickens with their head cut off.&#34;</p><p>Novogratz said he expects the total value of crypto assets to triple, or even quadruple, to between $6 trillion and $8 trillion in the coming years.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/crypto-trading-investing-tips-crypto-tokens-hodling-trader-scott-melker-2021-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">&#39;Wolf of All Streets&#39; crypto trader Scott Melker breaks down his strategy for making money using &#39;HODLing&#39; and 100X trade opportunities - and shares 5 under-the-radar tokens he thinks could explode</a></em></p><div around the same time.</p><p>This followed widespread protests against police brutality in the US after <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/derek-chauvin-verdict-george-floyd-death-2021-4\">George Floyd was killed by a Minneapolis police officer</a> who knelt on his neck for more than nine minutes.</p><p>Amazon <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-workers-accuse-company-hypocrisy-george-floyd-statement-2020-6\">workers criticized the company</a> for supporting the George Floyd protesters while continuing to flog its controversial technology to law enforcement.</p><p>Facial recognition is an increasingly popular tool that police use to track down criminals, terrorists, or illegal immigrants. But <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/24/technology/amazon-facial-technology-study.html\">numerous</a> <a href=\"https://www.aclu.org/blog/privacy-technology/surveillance-technologies/amazons-face-recognition-falsely-matched-28\">studies</a> indicate that Amazon&#39;s Rekognition is less adept at recognizing darker skin tones.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ai-experts-call-on-amazon-not-to-sell-rekognition-software-to-police-2019-4?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"a02bded39eb256db56757a68ceca59a5\">AI experts</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/aclu-amazon-investors-to-stop-firm-selling-rekognition-to-law-enforcement-2019-5?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"756d06c3c11c971101675ed855a914a6\">civil rights leaders</a> have said this disproportionately targets Black people and other people of color. The New York Times reported in December that three wrongful arrests of Black men had taken place in the US due to flawed facial recognition.</p><p>Amazon said in June it hoped a one year pause would allow Congress to create legislation that regulated the ethical use of facial recognition tools. Congress hasn&#39;t yet banned the technology. </p><p>Now, the retailer wants to extend the moratorium indefinitely.</p><p>Amazon didn&#39;t immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment.</p><p>&#34;This is a huge win for privacy and is the direct result of years of work by activists and advocates who have shed light on the dangerous use of this flawed technology,&#34; the American Civil Liberties Union <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ACLU/status/1394748759863660545\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">said in a statement on Twitter</a>.</p><p>&#34;We can&#39;t let dystopian technologies supercharge police abuse and cause further harm to Black and Brown communities,&#34; it said, adding that other companies must follow suit.</p><p>Despite Amazon&#39;s pause on sales of Rekognition, US police make widespread use of other surveillance technology sold by the retail giant, namely its doorbell camera arm Ring.</p><p>Reporting by Motherboard from 2019 onwards has <a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/j5wyjy/amazon-told-police-it-has-partnered-with-200-law-enforcement-agencies\">uncovered extensive partnerships</a> between US police departments and Ring to enable access home security footage, and one academic <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2021/may/18/amazon-ring-largest-civilian-surveillance-network-us\">recently described Ring</a> as a huge &#34;civilian surveillance network.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-extends-ban-police-facial-recognition-software-2021-5'>Business
