22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"Biden gave Republicans a Tuesday deadline for an infrastructure proposal. They missed it.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/republican-infrastructure-counter-offer-biden-capito-bipartisan-agreement-missed-deadline-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a52183e25d05001880c704?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Joe Biden Shelley Moore Capito in Oval Office White House\" height=\"2062\" width=\"2749\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Joe Biden meets with Sen. Shelley Moore Capito at the White House.\n<p class=\"copyright\">NICHOLAS KAMM/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>GOP lawmakers didn&#39;t make Biden a counter-offer to his infrastructure plan by his Tuesday deadline.</li>\n<li>They said Biden is still digesting their $568 billion plan and they&#39;ll hear from the White House this week.</li>\n<li>Democrats are increasingly calling on Biden to ditch negotiations and move forward without the GOP.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>After a group of Republican senators met with President Joe Biden last week to discuss their $568 billion counter-proposal to the president&#39;s infrastructure plan, he gave them a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/infrastructure-gop-plan-biden-counter-proposal-tuesday-deadline-2021-5\">Tuesday deadline</a> to bring forth a new offer. That never happened.</p><p>Republican senators, led by West Virginia Sen. Shelley Moore Capito, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/senate-republican-infrastructure-plan-breakdown-biden-2021-4\">introduced</a> the $568 billion proposal last month - significantly smaller than Biden&#39;s $4 trillion plan. It included funding mainly dedicated to physical infrastructure, like roads and bridges, and proposed funding the plan through potential &#34;user-fees,&#34; like a gas or road tax, instead of the corporate tax hikes the president pitched.</p><p>The meeting came and went between this group and Biden, Transportation Sec. Pete Buttigieg, and Commerce Sec. Gina Raimondo and a new plan wasn&#39;t introduced, with Capito telling reporters after the meeting that there was &#34;progress, but we still got a ways to go.&#34;</p><p>&#34;I think they&#39;re [Buttigieg and Raimondo] digesting what we proposed, and I think the plan is for them to react to that,&#34; Capito added.</p><p>Capito&#39;s office referred Insider to a readout of the meeting which said Capito felt &#34;encouraged,&#34; and the White House would follow up with the group later this week.</p><p>While a new plan wasn&#39;t brought to the table, Capito told reporters there was &#34;back and forth&#34; during the meeting on what it would take to carry out some of the measures in Biden&#39;s plan, and that while they did talk about methods to fund a plan, they didn&#39;t go too in depth on the matter because they first need to decide on what they&#39;re going to fund in the first place.</p><h2>Democrats want Biden to bypass the GOP</h2><p>Biden has repeatedly said he would like to reach a bipartisan agreement on infrastructure, and that he is willing to compromise on the scope and size of his plan. But Democratic lawmakers are concerned that the focus on bipartisanship is taking too much time away from passing urgent legislation.</p><p>On Monday, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/house-democrats-biden-infrastructure-legislation-bipartisan-agreeement-pramila-jayapal-2021-5\">59 House Democrats</a> sent a letter to Speaker of the House Nancy Pelosi and Senate Majority Leader Chuck Schumer urging them to bypass negotiations with Republicans and go even bigger on infrastructure investments, suggesting a <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/us-policy/2021/03/29/biden-infrastructure-taxes-spending-plan/\">$7 trillion</a> proposal that Biden campaigned on.</p><p>&#34;While bipartisan support is welcome, the pursuit of Republican votes cannot come at the expense of limiting the scope of popular investments,&#34; the Democrats wrote.</p><p>Biden and Republicans have expressed interest in striking some sort of bipartisan agreement by Memorial Day, but as Democrats are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/john-podesta-infrastructure-plan-biden-gop-progressives-bipartisan-2021-5\">increasingly</a> urging the president to leave the GOP behind and pass legislation, the only other route is budget reconciliation, which even some Democrats are weary of.</p><p>Sen. Sheldon Whitehouse of Rhode Island, for example, <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/05/19/biden-liberals-republicans-infrastructure-489418\">told</a> Politico that will using reconciliation to bypass Republicans would be &#34;quicker and easier,&#34; he said Democrats &#34;don&#39;t seem to have the votes for it,&#34; likely referring to moderate Democrat Sen. Joe Manchin of West Virginia&#39;s desire to have a bipartisan bill.</p><p>While Senate Minority Leader Mitch McConnell said the GOP&#39;s infrastructure plan could cost <a href=\"https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&rct=j&q=&esrc=s&source=web&cd=&cad=rja&uact=8&ved=2ahUKEwiExYvt-dXwAhUCKVkFHZSGBGsQFjAAegQIBBAD&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.businessinsider.com%2Fmitch-mcconnell-backtracks-on-infrastructure-red-line-price-tag-bipartisan-2021-5&usg=AOvVaw1vAxORou7985L52-ZEs_je1-5&#38;usg=AOvVaw1vAxORou7985L52-ZEs_je\">up to $800 billion</a>, that would still not be nearly enough for Democrats who want to include care-economy investments, like affordable housing and free community college, and if Democrats want to adhere to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nancy-pelosi-infrastructure-bill-july-4-biden-big-four-meeting-2021-5\">Pelosi&#39;s July 4 timeline</a> to bring a bill to the House floor, a bipartisan agreement looks unlikely.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/6086db953f0560001881c03c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"pelo tread\" height=\"1120\" width=\"1498\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Peloton</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Peloton has a new safety feature for customers that choose to keep its recalled Tread+ machine.</li>\n<li>Peloton issued a voluntary recall of its treadmills at the start of May after the CPC advised against using them.</li>\n<li>The new safety update will automatically lock the machine Tread+ has a new safety feature. </p><p>Peloton Tread+ customers will be asked to update their software when they next log on to the machine, and activate a new &#34;Tread Lock.&#34; This will lock the treadmill when it&#39;s not in use, or after 45 seconds of inactivity, and you&#39;ll need a password to unlock it.</p><p>As per Peloton <a href=\"https://support.onepeloton.com/hc/en-us/articles/360060884531-Tread-Lock\">instructions online</a>, published Tuesday, customers will set the password when they update the software.</p><p>This new safety feature comes after Peloton issued a recall of its high-tech running machines following reports that a child had died, and that several others were injured, while using the machine.</p><p>As this was a voluntary recall, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-recalls-treadmill-death-injuries-members-will-not-return-2021-5\">some customers opted to keep</a> the machine, and this new update is intended to make the machines safer for those customers. </p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-tread-customers-report-injury-malfunction-as-early-as-2019-2021-4?inline-read-more\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"dbb705aab28dc3fff28093e2afb9fb00\">Peloton just recalled its treadmill, but customers reported injuries and safety concerns as early as January 2019</a></em></p><p>A spokesperson for Peloton told Insider that the screen lock was only available on its Tread+ machine currently, but will be rolled out to the cheaper &#34;Tread&#34; version in the summer.  </p><p>Peloton issued a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-recalls-tread-treadmills-after-injury-reports-death-2021-5\">recall</a> of its treadmills following an investigation by the US Consumer Product Safety Commission (CPSC), which <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-peloton-treadmill-could-pose-safety-risks-child-death-cpsc-2021-4\">deemed its machines unsafe</a> and advised Peloton members to stop using them. </p><p>Despite this, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-recalls-treadmill-death-injuries-members-will-not-return-2021-5\">some Peloton treadmill users told Insider</a> that they had no plans to return the machine and get a refund.</p><p>&#34;I am NOT returning it. I love it, and even with an eight-year-old daughter and a dog in my two-bedroom apartment, it&#39;s not going anywhere,&#34; Tread+ owner Peter Shankman previously wrote in an email to Insider, adding that he has a rigorous safety routine in place. </p><p>&#34;I taught my daughter from the second I got it that she was never to go anywhere near it unless I was right there and gave her permission. Not even to stand on it,&#34; he said.</p><p>Whenever his $4,295 treadmill is not in use, Shankman said that he removes the safety key - another feature that prevents the machine from moving - and stores it in a place his daughter can&#39;t access.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (Mary Hanbury)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6086db953f0560001881c03c?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn51@2020_1/2021/05/19/14-56-02-399_7cd9713e1b76927e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn88@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-05-974_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=8giD_hbjBM4:sq18UoGrvRA:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn88@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-06-801_f2c1f4760f1afa28.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=8giD_hbjBM4:sq18UoGrvRA:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn11@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-05-141_faaa98f74544054d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn71@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-33-719_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=8giD_hbjBM4:sq18UoGrvRA:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn32@2020_1/2021/05/19/14-56-01-996_1a50e2a22644452f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/8giD_hbjBM4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn91@2020_1/2021/05/19/14-56-01-862_0eb11c630be7dd3b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436145852},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"Navy SEALs are refocusing to fight China and Russia. Here's what current and former members say they're up against.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-navy-seals-are-refocusing-to-fight-china-and-russia-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60087ed06d4c620018e410cb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Navy SEAL BUD/S Hell Week\" height=\"738\" width=\"1476\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Navy SEAL candidates during Basic Underwater Demolition/SEAL (BUD/S) training in Coronado, California, January 23, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy/PO1 Abe McNatt</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Naval Special Warfare Command is making strategic shift from counterterrorism operations to great-power competition.</li>\n<li>To take on new more capable foes - namely Russia and China - the command is retooling its forces to apply old skills to new challenges.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Recently, Rear Adm. H. Wyman Howard III, the top SEAL officer and a former commander of SEAL Team 6, testified in Congress and highlighted Naval Special Warfare Command&#39;s strategic shift from counterterrorism operations to great-power competition against near-peer competitors, such as Russia and China.</p><h2>A sea change</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e9f41635bd7a50d41544d60?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Navy SEAL graduation\" height=\"964\" width=\"1400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SEAL Qualification Training Class 336 at their graduation ceremony, April 15, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy/MCS 1st Class Anthony W. Walker</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Following his testimony, Howard told the <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/politics-osama-bin-laden-china-russia-government-and-politics-8f277ce1a284b227afcdcffabfb51ffc\" target=\"_top\">Associated Press</a> that Naval Special Warfare Command is looking to slash 30% of its SEAL platoons but increase the number of operators in each of the remaining platoons.</p><p>Now each SEAL Team will have six instead of eight platoons. It isn&#39;t clear, however, if the added troops will be SEAL operators or direct-support troops.</p><p>There are less than 3,000 active-duty SEALs right now, and a typical SEAL platoon is composed of 16 operators.</p><p>But each platoon is usually augmented by direct support personnel, such as cryptologists or Explosive Ordnance Disposal (EOD) technicians, and by other commandos, such as Air Force Pararescuemen or Combat Controllers, thus inflating the actual number of troops on target.</p><p>In his testimony, Howard revealed that there will be new courses and standards for SEAL officers and senior enlisted operators as a result of several scandals that have rocked the community.</p><p>Insider understands that all junior SEAL officers will be required to go through an ethics course. In addition to this mandatory course, Naval Special Warfare <a href=\"https://www.armed-services.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/20210428_NSWC%20Posture%20Statement_SASC-ETC-FINAL.pdf\" target=\"_top\">has introduced</a> a mid-level assessment process for officers eligible for higher command.</p><p>&#34;These changes are generally good as they enhance the tactical element and give us more punch downrange. And they make sense as we&#39;re gearing for a fight against actual, competent militaries and not just a bunch of ragtag fanatics,&#34; a SEAL operator told Insider.</p><p>&#34;Against the Chinese, we won&#39;t be worrying so much about small-arms fire as about their electronic- and cyber-warfare capabilities. CT [counterterrorism] ops are still dangerous, but they don&#39;t have the same risk as an op against a Chinese harbor,&#34; the SEAL operator added.</p><h2>Different but similar</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/605bc3f90d155e0019ef69b0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Navy SEAL Afghanistan\" height=\"1331\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Navy SEAL takes a defensive position in northern Zabul province, Afghanistan, April 10, 2010.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy/Chief MCS Jeremy L. Wood</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Throughout the Global War on Terror, US forces have enjoyed undisputed air superiority, allowing conventional and special-operations units to operate much more freely than they would in a contested environment.</p><p>However, in a potential conflict with China or Russia, US forces might not enjoy the same advantages.</p><p>For example, understanding the conventional might of the US military, China has pursued the anti-access/anti-denial (A2/AD) concept in an attempt to negate the US Navy&#39;s capabilities in the Pacific in general but especially around Taiwan, a country that China sees as a breakaway province and wants to reabsorb.</p><p>To that end, Beijing has been building and fortifying man-made islands in the South China Sea, where many countries dispute China&#39;s expansive claims. These islands essentially act as pickets, preventing US aircraft carriers from getting within range and diminishing their usefulness.</p><p>In addition, earlier this year, US Indo-Pacific Command sounded the alarm about the shifting balance of power in its area of operations. China, the Pentagon warned, <a href=\"https://www.sandboxx.us/blog/the-chinese-military-will-outmatch-the-us-in-the-pacific-by-2025/\" target=\"_top\">will militarily outmatch</a> US forces in the Pacific by 2025.</p><p>Although this assessment didn&#39;t consider US and allied reinforcements from other areas of operations, it shows the threat level.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a46594f27b4c001944538a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Navy SEAL Special Boat Team\" height=\"1499\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Navy SEALs train with Special Boat Team 12 to board gas and oil platforms from a moving vessel, July 28, 2011.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy/PO3 Adam Henderson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In such an environment, Naval Special Warfare has all the potential to shine. Indeed, in case of a conflict with China, they are the logical go-to choice for any special-operations missions.</p><p>&#34;Honestly, and although lots of people in the community might not like to admit it, great power competition and a conflict with a nation-state like China or Russia or even North Korea and Iran suits the [SEAL] Teams&#39; DNA better,&#34; a former SEAL officer told Insider.</p><p>Moscow has been pursuing a similar A2/AD strategy in annexed Crimea, with the Russian military making the peninsula a fortress. Operations in the Black Sea region around Crimea, like the islands and littorals of the Pacific, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/navy-seals-swcc-training-for-land-water-combat-near-russia-2021-5\" target=\"_top\">would play to the SEAL Teams&#39; strengths</a>.</p><p>&#34;CT [Counterterrorism] is cool and a great recruitment tool-who doesn&#39;t love kicking in doors and shooting bad guys in the face?-but the Teams are more than that, a lot more, actually,&#34; the former SEAL officer said.</p><p>&#34;Our forefathers, the UDT [underwater demolition team] frogmen, were established during World War II to do underwater demolitions and hydrographic recon. From the beaches of Normandy during D-Day to Iwo Jima and Okinawa, frogmen paved the way for the Marines and the Army,&#34; the former officer added. &#34;In a future conflict with a big power, we would end up doing essentially similar missions. For sure, they will be more technologically advanced, but the gist remains the same. People [in the community] need to understand that and embrace it.&#34;</p><h2>Old skills, new missions</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/59e4c0b506fca06abc6c8225?format=jpeg\" alt=\"us navy seal submarine delivery vehicle SDV\" height=\"812\" width=\"1259\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SEAL Delivery Vehicle Team Two members launch a SEAL Delivery Vehicle from Los Angeles-class attack sub USS Philadelphia.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy photo by Chief Photographer&#39;s Mate Andrew McKaskle</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>To be sure, there is a degree of overlap between skill-sets used in counterterrorism operations and those that will be required against a near-peer threat.</p><p>For example, preparing the intelligence for and executing direct-action missions, such as raids or ambushes, will be the same despite the targets being different.</p><p>China, moreover, has the largest navy in the world, with about <a href=\"https://www.sandboxx.us/blog/us-navy-would-face-a-massive-770-ship-force-in-a-pacific-fight-with-china/\" target=\"_top\">750 vessels</a> of varying tonnage and capabilities. Naval Special Warfare&#39;s SEAL Delivery Vehicle - mini-subs that can transport SEALs close to a target without alerting the enemy - is ideal for operations to restrict those vessels&#39; movement, such as by blocking ports, or even to sink them.</p><p>But Naval Special Warfare&#39;s smallest community, the Special Warfare Combatant-Craft Crewmen (SWCCs), who specialize in direct action, reconnaissance, and ship-boarding operations, adds a lot to the equation.</p><p>&#34;Frankly, I think the SWCC community in many ways is designed for a near-peer environment conflict,&#34; a former SWCC operator told Insider. &#34;The Special Boat Teams are one of the only elite maritime special operations units in the world. Our mainstay is over-the-beach direct-action operations, coastal reconnaissance, and VBSS. These three items would be a huge element in any major great-power competition.&#34;</p><p>&#34;With the technologically advanced boats and weapons at the Boat Team&#39;s disposal, they can effectively wage war against a modern-day enemy. SWCC&#39;s concentrate on speed, stealth, and firepower. These attributes make them extremely dangerous and specialized,&#34; the former SWCC operator added.</p><p><em>Stavros Atlamazoglou is a defense journalist specializing in special operations, a Hellenic Army veteran (national service with the 575th Marine Battalion and Army HQ), and a Johns Hopkins University graduate.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a If you'd like to take part in all of the deals and discounts, you can register for a 30-day free trial. After that, you'll be charged $12.99 or $119 per year as a Prime member.</p><p>Sign up to be a Prime member <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/amazonprime?_encoding=UTF8&#38;hvadid=381655816555&#38;hvdev=c&#38;hvexid=&#38;hvnetw=g&#38;hvpone=&#38;hvpos=&#38;hvptwo=&#38;hvqmt=b&#38;hvrand=15335622783904615915&#38;ref=pd_sl_5bvjl7yi1_e&#38;tag=googhydr-20&#38;_encoding=UTF8&#38;tag=biipg_051821_amazon-prime-day-most-popular-products-20&#38;linkCode=ur2&#38;linkId=80c43b6989a8cf3af0750024ff25a1fb&#38;camp=1789&#38;creative=9325\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">here</a>.</p><hr /><h3>How long will Amazon Prime Day last?</h3><p>Typically, it's been a two-day sale. Originally, however, it began as a single-day event. 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"10 simple strategies to help you be more productive and focused while working from home","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-best-tips-for-improving-your-work-from-home-lifestyle-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1c0bcf27b4c0019444c06?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Work from home\" height=\"1665\" width=\"2221\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The author working at home.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A year into the pandemic, working from home is preferred by many employees.</li>\n<li>But working remotely can still be very monotonous. </li>\n<li>Try making simple tweaks to your routine, like setting reminders to take breaks. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>I&#39;ve gone through a complete remote-work evolution since I started working from home last March. </p><p>It can be tough finding ways to be efficient, without also increasing the risk of burnout. From turning my fireplace mantel into a standing desk, to doing yoga while proofreading for work, I&#39;ve tried almost everything to keep myself productive.</p><p>And these challenges might be here to stay. Over a year after the CDC announced the pandemic, effectively shutting down the US, a <a href=\"https://news.harvard.edu/gazette/story/2021/03/survey-reveals-what-worked-about-online-work/\" rel=\"noopener\">Harvard survey</a> revealed that 81% of the workforce either doesn&#39;t want to return to the office or would prefer a hybrid schedule moving forward. At least 27% hopes to continue working remotely full-time.</p><p>Remote work has many benefits - no waking up early, no morning commute, and no reason to get dressed in business attire. But it can also be a <a href=\"https://www.gallup.com/workplace/323228/remote-workers-facing-high-burnout-turn-around.aspx\" rel=\"noopener\">challenge;</a> remote workers during the pandemic often struggle with the monotony of logging on from home every day. </p><p>If you&#39;re struggling with engagement at work right now, here are some ways to freshen up your work-from-home lifestyle to help you be more productive. </p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\t1. Change your notification sounds\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1c796f27b4c0019444c0f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Changing Slack notifications\" height=\"388\" width=\"720\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Changing the notification sound on Slack.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Here's a riddle for you. What do you hear a million times a day, but never really notice anymore? Your notifications.&#160;</p><p>Instead of a spoken \"Hey, can you help me with this?,\" you got an audible \"ping\" with every new alert, instilling an almost Pavlovian response to check your inbox or direct messages. After awhile, though, that knee-jerk reaction may have dulled with time as the sound started to pass right below your threshold of awareness.&#160;</p><p>To liven up your communications again, try changing your notification sound every 2-3 months. This could be the notifications on your phone, <a href=\"https://slack.com/help/articles/201355156-Configure-your-Slack-notifications#sound-and-appearance\" rel=\"noopener\">on Slack</a>, for email, etc. Whatever you need to do to press the reset button in your mind.</p>\n\t2. Switch out your computer wallpaper\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1c996f27b4c0019444c15?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Changing wallpaper on Macbook\" height=\"449\" width=\"599\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Switching out computer wallpapers.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>You're likely going to be staring at your screen all day long.</p><p>Switching out your wallpaper can be a welcome change. It could be a naturescape, a family photo, a picture of your dog.</p><p>You'll be pleasantly surprised at how something so simple can make you feel exponentially more engaged throughout the work day. When you find yourself noticing the picture less and less, it's time to change it up again.</p>\n\t3. Download applications and extensions to avoid non-work-related internet usage\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1cc0ff27b4c0019444c1b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Downloading applications onto computer\" height=\"517\" width=\"689\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Download applications and extensions when possible to avoid unnecessary internet searches.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>We've all done it &#8212; opening a tab to look something up for work and somehow finding yourself on YouTube watching Binging With Babish's latest video. To avoid these little excursions, try downloading applications and extensions when possible.&#160;</p><p>For instance, if you work primarily on social media, download the Twitter application on your laptop to reduce the likelihood that you'll get lost down the Google rabbit hole. When you're doing the same tasks every day, it can be far too easy to meander, especially when you know no one's watching.</p>\n\t4. Play around with different style settings\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1cda3f27b4c0019444c1c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Changing themes on Google Chrome\" height=\"281\" width=\"640\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Try switching up themes and style settings on your computer.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Whether you have a Mac or a PC, you'll likely have the option to customize your computer's style settings. Even if you're just switching from Light mode to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-turn-on-dark-mode-on-windows\" rel=\"noopener\">Dark mode</a>, that small change will grab your attention every time you open your computer.</p><p>You may also be able to choose between an array of accent colors or customize settings all the way down to the font. On <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-google-chrome\">Google Chrome</a>, for example, you can <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-change-google-theme\" rel=\"noopener\">choose between a variety of themes</a>, or even create one.&#160;</p><p>Use your imagination with these style settings. It's a fun and easy way to explore and curate your professional niche at home.</p>\n\t5. Utilize organization tools\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1c28bf27b4c0019444c0b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tab groups on Chrome\" height=\"432\" width=\"576\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The group tab function in Google Chrome.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Both <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-group-tabs-in-google-chrome\" rel=\"noopener\">Google Chrome</a> and <a href=\"https://www.ghacks.net/2020/12/05/microsoft-edge-gets-chromiums-tab-groups-feature/\" rel=\"noopener\">Microsoft Edge</a> offer a tab group function, allowing you to combine tabs to keep related pages together in one place. The beauty of this feature is that it lets you condense what could otherwise be an overwhelming slew of seemingly random browser tabs into more digestible chunks.</p><p>This function even gives you the options of naming individual tab groups, color-coding each group, and expanding or collapsing groups to free up space in your tabs bar. In addition, Google Chrome offers an <a href=\"https://www.digitalinformationworld.com/2020/12/good-news-you-can-now-enjoy-google.html\" rel=\"noopener\">Auto Tab Groups Creation feature</a>, which will automatically group similar tabs together.&#160;</p><p>Just as you may save specific sites or pages in your bookmarks bar, these features add an additional layer to keeping your browser visually neat and compartmentalized. If you're someone who thrives on finding new ways to organize, the tab group function may be right up your alley.</p>\n\t6. Set reminders to take breaks\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1ceadf27b4c0019444c1d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Time Out break reminder\" height=\"280\" width=\"640\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Time Out application&#39;s inspirational quotes break function.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>When you first started working from home, you may have been diligent about getting up and moving around. Maybe you took walks, or just got a quick stretch in. But as time has gone by, perhaps your activity levels have taken a nosedive.</p><p>It can be far too easy to let eight hours slide by without any substantial movement or activity, especially when you're in the comfort of your own home. Rather than rely on instinct to pull yourself away from work, try downloading an application that will actively remind you to step back, get up, and move.</p><p>For example, the <a href=\"https://apps.apple.com/us/app/time-out-break-reminders/id402592703?mt=12\" rel=\"noopener\">Time Out</a> application lets you customize how often you want to be reminded to take a break, and for how long you want that break to last. Once you've set up the timing of your breaks, you can choose how you want to be notified it's time to take your breather.</p><p>There are other ways of reminding yourself it's time to take a break, like investing in a <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Fidus-Leakproof-Motivational-Sports-Green-Gradient/dp/B08BNPC1B7/ref=sr_1_11?crid=3FPEZLP3RJQB5&#38;dchild=1&#38;keywords=water+bottle+with+time+marker&#38;qid=1621254293&#38;sprefix=water+bottle+with+time%2Caps%2C183&#38;sr=8-11\" rel=\"noopener\">time-marked water bottle.</a> The tick marks on the bottle will help you keep track of how much water you're drinking, but can also serve the dual function of indicating when you should get up and move.&#160;</p><p>Spend some time researching options to find the one that fits best.</p>\n\t7. Develop your own hybrid work schedule\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1c0131b5cea0019c453fe?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Working at a coffee shop\" height=\"1874\" width=\"2498\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The author working at a local cafe.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Rather than working from home all day, every day, try working from a new location. That could be a local coffee shop, a coworking space, or maybe even your office. For example, make a plan to spend alternating days at home and at a cafe.</p><p>But schedule your <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-zoom-guide\">Zoom</a> calls for the days you're at home. The stranger sitting at the table next to you almost certainly doesn't want to hear you explain to your coworkers the details of your company's Q1 finance report.</p><p>Adopting a hybrid schedule is especially accommodating for those who miss some of the social nuances of an office workspace. This way, you'll get your work done while also getting to see some new faces.</p>\n\t8. Come up with a snack plan\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a25dc7f27b4c0019444cb3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Making a smoothie\" height=\"1809\" width=\"2412\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The author prepares a premade frozen smoothie mix.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Just like you shouldn't go grocery shopping on an empty stomach, you also shouldn't start working from home without a snack plan. It can be far too easy when you're sitting at home to munch on some less savory or fulfilling foods. Start preparing in advance by keeping protein bars within reach, or making smoothie mixes and storing them in the freezer for easy blendability.&#160;</p><p>I've become addicted in recent months to the <a href=\"https://happymoneysaver.com/smoothie-freezer-packs/\" rel=\"noopener\">Quick and Easy Smoothie Freezer Packs</a> from Happy Money Saver. I make a bunch every weekend, pull one out when I need a quick pick-me-up, and I'm right back to work. It's a great way to get a speedy and nutritional boost, and you can customize them however you like.</p>\n\t9. Subscribe to a monthly service\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1bdddf27b4c0019444c02?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Receiving a delivery at home\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The author receiving a package at home.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Subscribing to a service that serves your professional needs can help add some excitement to your daily routine.&#160;</p><p>If you're a big coffee drinker, try a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trade-coffee-review\" rel=\"noopener\">subscription to Trade Coffee</a>, which compares your personal tastes to its over 400 varieties of coffee to deliver an assortment of brews to your door. Or, if you're someone who thrives on taking detailed written notes throughout the workday, maybe give <a href=\"https://clothandpaper.com/\" rel=\"noopener\">Cloth &#38; Paper</a> a gander. Every month, you'll receive a box full of unique goodies, from notebooks, to planners, to pens.</p><p>Having something on the calendar to look forward to each month will instill a sense of structure that can be easily lacking when working remotely.</p>\n\t10. Invest in you\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1be311b5cea0019c453fd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Making a cappuccino\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The author makes a cappuccino at home.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Macchi/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Beyond just subscribing to a monthly delivery service, set aside some time to invest in yourself. At this point, you've more than likely nailed down a work-from-home routine, but there are always ways to zhuzh things up.</p><p>If you're still buying your latte every morning at your local Starbucks, invest in an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-espresso-machine\" rel=\"noopener\">espresso machine</a> so you can try your hand at making your own at home.</p><p>If you just want to dabble with your inner barista skills without forking out a ton of money, there are plenty of affordable options. I bought this <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Espresso-Machine-Cappuccino-Frother-Carafe/dp/B08X1NGSLK/ref=sr_1_1?crid=2ILWMFOSBKIP5&#38;dchild=1&#38;keywords=sowtech+espresso+machine&#38;qid=1621217286&#38;sprefix=sowtech+es%2Caps%2C179&#38;sr=8-1\" rel=\"noopener\">SOWTECH machine</a> for around $60 on Amazon and it's been a great way to dip my toes without committing to a big, shiny contraption.&#160;</p><p>And if you work out before, after, or even during the workday, perhaps consider purchasing a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-fitness-tracker\" rel=\"noopener\">fitness watch</a> so you can track your progress day-to-day. I've done all my workouts at home over the past year and my fitness watch serves as a visual reminder that I'm still moving and being active by counting my steps, individual workouts, etc.</p><p>It's little things like these that make it feel less like you're trying to force your work and home life together, but rather that the two are now one and the same.</p>\n</div><div src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a4ffccf27b4c0019445425?format=jpeg\" alt=\"target shopper\" height=\"999\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jessica Rinaldi/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Target shares rose as much as 3% on Wednesday after the company&#39;s first-quarter results jumped past Wall Street&#39;s estimates. </li>\n<li>Adjusted earnings of $3.69 a share blew past the $2.25 a share estimate from Refinitiv. </li>\n<li>Digital same-store sales grew by 50% during the three-month period. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/tgt-stock\">Target</a> shares climbed as much as 3% on Wednesday following first-quarter results that showed earnings surged as shoppers took advantage of the company&#39;s same-day services.</p><p>The retailer said its adjusted earnings were $3.69 a share, well beyond the $2.25 a share forecast generated from a Refinitiv poll of analysts. Adjusted earnings soared from $0.59 a share a year ago.</p><p>Total revenue increased by 23% to $24.2 billion in the three months ended May 1 from $19.62 billion a year ago, outpacing the $21.81 billion consensus estimate.</p><p>The stock has gained more than 70% over the past year as the retailer, like others, has dealt with challenges brought on by the COVID-19 pandemic.</p><p>Target said growth in the most recent period stemmed in part from a 50% climb in same-store digital sales, including more than 90% rise in same-day services such as drive-up and in-store order pickup and Shipt grocery deliveries.</p><p>Shoppers purchased more apparel and home goods items, which helped the company gain more than $1 billion in market share during the quarter. </p><p>&#34;[We&#39;re] confident in continued comp growth in the second quarter and through the remainder of the year, as well as a healthy full-year operating margin rate,&#34; Target said in its earnings report. </p><div Mozée)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60a4ffccf27b4c0019445425?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn84@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-03-070_d304cb9d883765cc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn88@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-05-974_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uggZdfmB-vY:pgRiwqCMwKk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn84@2020_1/2021/05/19/14-56-02-775_2a0375979e90ed21.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uggZdfmB-vY:pgRiwqCMwKk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn36@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-07-824_0cc41b79e970a8ee.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn71@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-33-719_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uggZdfmB-vY:pgRiwqCMwKk:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn52@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-02-988_f22ae53826876c2d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/uggZdfmB-vY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn99@2020_5/2021/05/19/14-56-00-984_e05733da755ce215.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436145860},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"Inside Netflix's plan to create 'spectacle' TV and major events like 'Jupiter's Legacy' and 'The Queen's Gambit'","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/inside-netflixs-spectacle-tv-push-which-includes-jupiters-legacy-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3d3631b5cea0019c4576c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sweeth tooth netflix\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1934\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;Sweet Tooth.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Netflix</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Netflix introduced a spectacle and events TV division last year, led by exec Peter Friedlander.</li>\n<li>Friedlander broke down the difference between spectacle and event programming.</li>\n<li>He also discussed shows that fall under his purview, like &#34;Jupiter&#39;s Legacy&#34; and the upcoming &#34;Sweet Tooth.&#34;</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The worlds of Netflix&#39;s latest comic-book shows, its upcoming &#34;<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9zG9RuJb3QU\">Sweet Tooth</a>&#34; and recent hit &#34;Jupiter&#39;s Legacy,&#34; are very different.</p><p>&#34;Jupiter&#39;s Legacy&#34; is about the world&#39;s first superheroes struggling to pass on their decades-old code of values to their superpowered children as their enemies become more dangerous. &#34;Sweet Tooth&#34; is a fantasy series where many children have been born as half-human, half-animal &#34;hybrids.&#34; Gus, a human-deer boy, sets out on a journey across a post-apocalyptic America looking for answers about himself as he&#39;s being hunted.</p><p>But Netflix&#39;s Peter Friedlander, who runs the team behind them, talks about both with the same sense of wonder.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s fun for me to mine these worlds that do have existing fandoms that you hope you can ignite around a visual medium and expand upon them,&#34; Friedlander told Insider during a recent interview ahead of the release of &#34;Sweet Tooth&#34; on June 4.</p><p>Both shows are part of Netflix&#39;s grander content ambitions as it looks to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/list-of-netflix-upcoming-franchises-events-spectacles-tv-movies-2021-3\">build bankable franchises or &#34;spectacle&#34; programming</a> that can compete with established Hollywood IP from the likes of Disney and WarnerMedia. Netflix said <a href=\"https://variety.com/2021/tv/news/netflix-2021-content-spend-17-billion-1234955953/\">it would spend $17 billion on content</a> this year, up from $11.8 billion last year when the pandemic slowed production.</p><p>&#34;The thing that many studios are able to do is create great franchises,&#34; Netflix&#39;s co-CEO Reed Hastings told The Hollywood Reporter in September, when asked <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/netflix-wants-to-build-franchises-like-star-wars-harry-potter-2020-9\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"ea9eff0e8aa8649d4298668716bb88f7\">what Netflix could learn from Hollywood</a>. &#34;We&#39;re making great progress on that with &#39;Stranger Things&#39; and other properties, but compared to &#39;Harry Potter&#39; and &#39;Star Wars,&#39; we&#39;ve got a long way to go.&#34;</p><p>Friedlander is helping Netflix get there.</p><h2>How Netflix defines a spectacle or event series</h2><p>Friedlander joined the company in 2011 as its first employee dedicated to original series; a decade later, after playing an essential role in Netflix hits like &#34;House of Cards&#34; and &#34;The Haunting of Hill House,&#34; he&#39;s overseeing a new spectacle and event TV division introduced last year to help Netflix achieve its lofty goals (Kelly Luegenbiehl leads a new franchise TV team).</p><p>Friedlander described the content under his team as being in two buckets: visual-effects driven, IP driven fantasy, sci-fi, and action programming (spectacle TV) and prestige limited series like &#34;The Queen&#39;s Gambit&#34; and &#34;When They See Us&#34; (event TV).</p><p>Friedlander said that his team is responsible for scouting IP with potential to turn into shows, but they also hear pitches from creators. The team is composed of directors, managers, and associates across the original series division, and supported by other teams like business affairs, which negotiates contracts.</p><p>&#34;There is no checklist,&#34; Friedlander said of the content he looks for. &#34;It&#39;s not just me, but a number of talented, passionate superfans inside Netflix that are constantly mining IP or hearing pitches from storytellers that are so riveting they seem undeniable.&#34;</p><p>While Friedlander&#39;s shows don&#39;t technically start out as &#34;franchises,&#34; he said that the two teams - spectacle/events and franchises - will often work together. Netflix thinks about franchise shows as those that have spinoff potential, like the hit fantasy series &#34;The Witcher.&#34; Netflix is already developing a prequel series, called &#34;The Witcher: Blood Origin,&#34; and an anime movie.</p><p>&#34;I&#39;m hoping that the spectacle shows we&#39;re creating could one day become franchises,&#34; Friedlander said. &#34;The franchise team focuses on building those out.&#34;</p><p>What&#39;s most important to him in a story is whether a show is relatable, even if it&#39;s about a family of superheroes or a deer-human hybrid. </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s about the ability to emphasize with a character you didn&#39;t think that you would,&#34; he said. &#34;I&#39;m always looking to be put in other people&#39;s shoes and look through other people&#39;s eyes.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/609edaaaf27b4c00194449de?format=jpeg\" alt=\"jupiter&#39;s legacy\" height=\"1378\" width=\"2012\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;Jupiter&#39;s Legacy.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Netflix</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Netflix is leaning into genre like never before</h2><p>Netflix had 90 TV shows in early development or production based on books, comics, manga, or video games as of March, according to the research firm Ampere Analysis. Book adaptations lead with 60, and the remaining 30 were comic, manga, and game adaptations.</p><p>Some of those adaptations are projects that Friedlander and the events/spectacle team are overseeing. Here are a few:</p><ul><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/netflix-adapting-the-three-body-problem-game-of-thrones-duo-2020-9\">&#34;The Three-Body Problem,&#34;</a> based on the sci-fi novel by the Chinese author Liu Cixin. </li><li>A live-action &#34;Avatar: The Last Airbender&#34; series.</li><li>Tim Burton&#39;s &#34;Wednesday,&#34; based on the Addams Family&#39;s Wednesday Addams.</li><li>&#34;Cowboy Bebop,&#34; based on the anime series of the same name.</li><li>&#34;Vikings: Valhalla,&#34; a spin-off of History Channel&#39;s &#34;Vikings.&#34;</li><li>&#34;Assassin&#39;s Creed,&#34; based on the Ubisoft video-game franchise.</li></ul><p>Millarworld, the comic-book company founded by Mark Millar, is also under Friedlander&#39;s purview. Netflix bought it in 2017 in its first acquisition to develop content based on Millar&#39;s comics. The first was &#34;Jupiter&#39;s Legacy,&#34; which spent a week at the top of Netflix&#39;s daily lists of its most popular shows in the US earlier this month.</p><p>&#34;We knew we had something special when a team of superheroes is arguing at the dining table and then going off to fight a villain,&#34; Friedlander said. </p><p>&#34;Jupiter&#39;s Legacy&#34; is only the beginning for Millarworld at Netflix.</p><p>Millar has a board in his office with the next five years mapped out, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/netflixs-mark-millar-on-jupiters-legacy-and-millarworld-plans-2021-5\">he told Insider earlier this month</a>. The plans include &#34;American Jesus,&#34; about a teenager who discovers he&#39;s the resurrected Jesus Christ, and &#34;The Magic Order,&#34; which was postponed due to the pandemic but that Millar called a &#34;top priority&#34; along with &#34;Jupiter&#39;s Legacy.&#34; </p><p>&#34;We were drawn to the breadth of Mark&#39;s creations and stories,&#34; Friedlander said. &#34;With his existing IP as well as the stories yet to be told, we knew it was a really great opportunity to have him as a partner.&#34;</p><p>Next up for Friedlander&#39;s team is &#34;Sweeth Tooth,&#34; based on the post-apocalyptic DC comic by Jeff Lemire, which he described as a &#34;fairy tale&#34; with elements of drama, adventure, and sci-fi.</p><p>&#34;It has a real sense of adventure about it, but it also has a sense of hope and wonder,&#34; Friedlander said. &#34;Gus&#39; journey is both an emotional one as well as an adventurous one. As people experience the show it&#39;ll be like peeling back layers of an onion - there&#39;s something new with each episode.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Donald Trump and a photo of the Arizona ballot recount.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Arizona election auditors said Tuesday they&#39;d found files that were initially thought to be missing.</li>\n<li>Trump had seized on claims of missing voter data to push his election fraud &#34;Big Lie.&#34; </li>\n<li>The GOP-commissioned Arizona recount has been heavily mocked and criticized.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Auditors conducting the Republican-commissioned recount of 2020 election votes in Arizona&#39;s Maricopa County have found files of voter data that former President Donald Trump falsely claimed had been destroyed. </p><p>In a statement last week, Trump seized on a claim by auditors that data they subpoenaed while conducting the recount had gone missing as he pushed his conspiracy theory that last year&#39;s election was stolen from him.</p><p>&#34;The entire Database of Maricopa County in Arizona has been DELETED!&#34; Trump wrote at the time, claiming that journalists were too afraid to cover the story.</p><p>The statement had drawn a withering response from Maricopa County Recorder Stephen Richer, a Republican, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gop-election-official-in-arizona-county-recount-trump-is-unhinged-2021-5\">who had called the statement &#34;unhinged.&#34;</a></p><p>But on Tuesday it turned out that the missing data had been found. Ben Cotton, one of the auditing officials, told state senators that the files had been located on different computer hard drives to the ones they had been searching, <a href=\"https://news3lv.com/news/nation-world/arizona-auditors-backtrack-say-no-election-data-destroyed\">the Associated Press reported</a>.<a href=\"https://twitter.com/News3LV/status/1394873063724916738?s=20\"></a></p><p>Collins went on to describe Trump&#39;s claim that files were deleted as a &#34;moot point,&#34; the AP reported.</p><p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/maricopacounty/status/1394759892737552385?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1394759892737552385%7Ctwgr%5E%7Ctwcon%5Es1_&ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.businessinsider.com%2Farizona-recount-auditors-find-file-trump-claimed-was-destroyed-2021-521-5\">In a Tuesday tweet</a>, Maricopa County officials criticized the auditors for making the baseless accusation about missing data in the first place. </p><p>&#34;Just want to underscore that AZ Senate&#39;s @ArizonaAudit account accused Maricopa County of deleting files- which would be a crime- then a day after our technical letter explained they were just looking in the wrong place,&#34; the tweet said.</p><p>&#34;All of a sudden &#39;auditors&#39; have recovered the files,&#34; officials said.</p><p>The ballot recount, which was commissioned by the Republican-controlled Arizona Senate in April, has been embroiled in allegations of mismanagement and partisan bias for weeks. State Republican officials, the Arizona secretary of state, and the Justice Department have all raised concerns.</p><p>The state GOP claims that the recount is necessary as part of an investigation into tightening election integrity, but critics, including Maricopa&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/arizona-vote-recount-gop-led-elections-board-says-sham-2021-5\">GOP-controlled election board, have described it as a sham,</a> driven by the desire to give credibility to Trump&#39;s election-fraud conspiracy theories. </p><p>At a Tuesday meeting, Arizona Senate President Karen Fann <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/maricopa-county-audit-senate/2021/05/18/b6fab370-b816-11eb-a5fe-bb49dc89a248_story.html\">said</a> that despite criticism of the audit, it would go ahead.</p><p>The audit was scheduled to be wrapped up on May 14, but is now expected to go on for several more weeks. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (small)</bi-shortcode><p>The iPad Pro has always been Apple&#39;s most powerful tablet, but the company is taking that approach to the next level with its latest model. </p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">new iPad Pro</a>, which launches in the second half of May and starts at $800 for the 11-inch model, runs on Apple&#39;s M1 chip, the same powerful processor found inside the latest MacBook Pro and MacBook Air.</p><p>Compared to last year&#39;s version, the 11-inch iPad Pro I&#39;ve been testing also comes with optional 5G connectivity, a better webcam with Apple&#39;s new Center Stage feature, Thunderbolt support, and choices for more storage capacity. </p><p>All told, the addition of the M1 chip along with these improvements makes the iPad faster, longer-lasting, and more useful as a work device than before. Yet it still has limitations that prevent it from truly replacing your laptop, so it&#39;s better-suited for creatives rather than those with more traditional workflows. </p><p>Still, for creative professionals, the M1 chip is likely to open up a whole new set of possibilities. height: 21px;\">8GB or 16GB</td></tr><tr style=\"height: 21px;\"><td style=\"width: 50%; height: 21px;\">Authentication</td><td style=\"width: 50%; height: 21px;\">Face ID</td></tr><tr style=\"height: 21px;\"><td style=\"width: 50%; height: 21px;\">Colors</td><td style=\"width: 50%; height: 21px;\">Silver or Space Gray</td></tr></tbody></table><h2>Display and design</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3f7fb1b5cea0019c45852?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple’s 2021 iPad Pro has the new M1 chip\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Apple&#39;s 2021 iPad Pro with M1 (11-inch) has a similar design as its predecessor\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">11-inch iPad Pro</a> comes with a vibrant screen that packs 264 pixels per inch, just like the iPad Air, 12.9-inch iPad Pro, and previous-generation iPad Pro. Apple&#39;s new mini-LED display, which should enable better contrast, is only available on the latest larger-sized iPad Pro. </p><p>The biggest differences between the screens on the 11-inch iPad Pro and iPad Air is that the Pro&#39;s display is slightly larger, brighter, and includes Apple&#39;s ProMotion technology. This boosts the refresh rate up to 120Hz for smoother scrolling and faster responsiveness. </p><p>But it isn&#39;t noticeable enough to play a big role in your buying decision. Scrolling seems a bit faster, but using the second-generation Apple Pencil to sketch and color on the iPad Air generally feels as smooth as it does on the new iPad Pro. </p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">new iPad Pro</a> also has the same slim design as its predecessor. That&#39;s to say it has a sleek metal build with flat edges, making it extremely compact and portable. But unlike the colorful iPad Air, the iPad Pro only comes in silver and space gray.</p><h2>Performance</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3f8471b5cea0019c45853?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple’s 2021 iPad Pro has the new M1 chip and works with Apple Pencil\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Apple&#39;s 2021 iPad Pro with M1 (11-inch) with the newest Apple Pencil\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Pro</a>&#39;s M1 chip is impressively fast when it comes to processing video and photo edits. That&#39;s important for a device like this, which Apple has been pitching towards photographers, video editors, artists, designers, architects, and really anyone who works with 3D renderings.</p><p>In one test, the M1-equipped iPad Pro exported a 10-minute 4K video to 1080p using Adobe Premiere Rush in nearly half the amount of time it took for the iPad Air to accomplish the same task. It also beat last year&#39;s 12.9-inch iPad Pro by about 20 seconds. Exporting the same video on a Dell XPS 13 running on an 11th-generation Intel Core i7 chip took nearly 20 minutes.</p><p>The new iPad Pro was also a hair faster at exporting a 4.7MB photo using Adobe Lightroom, as shown in the results below.</p><table style=\"border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; height: 85px;\" border=\"1\"><tbody><tr style=\"height: 43px;\"><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 43px;\"> </td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 43px;\"><strong>Apple iPad Pro (11-inch, 2021)</strong></td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 43px;\"><strong>Apple iPad Air (2020)</strong></td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 43px;\"><strong>Apple iPad Pro (12.9-inch 2020)</strong></td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 43px;\"><strong>Dell XPS 13</strong></td></tr><tr style=\"height: 21px;\"><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\"><strong>Video Export</strong></td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">3 minutes, 25 seconds</td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">3 minutes, 45 seconds</td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">5 minutes, 55 seconds</td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">19 minutes, 58 seconds</td></tr><tr style=\"height: 21px;\"><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\"><strong>Photo Export</strong></td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">1.4 seconds</td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">2 seconds</td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">1.8 seconds</td><td style=\"width: 20%; height: 21px;\">3.2 seconds</td></tr></tbody></table><p>The jump in speed compared to Apple&#39;s older iPads is certainly notable. But it&#39;s really the way app developers put the M1 chip&#39;s power to use in their apps that will make the iPad Pro stand out. For example, the music composition app StaffPad is updating its app with a feature only available on M1 devices that automatically detects notes as you&#39;re playing an instrument.</p><p>It&#39;s features like this that showcase Apple&#39;s intentions for the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Pro</a> as a computing device. Although I&#39;ve always appreciated the iPad Pro for its speed, battery life, and compact design, I&#39;ve never really understood Apple&#39;s vision for it as a new type of computer. That seems poised to change now that the M1 chip has made its way to the iPad Pro, as apps like StaffPad are proving.</p><h2>Productivity</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3f9791b5cea0019c45857?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple’s 2021 iPad Pro has the company’s M1 chip\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Apple&#39;s 2021 iPad Pro with M1 (11-inch) with the Magic Keyboard\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>But don&#39;t get the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">iPad Pro</a> if you&#39;re really looking for a traditional laptop experience. Computers that run on a desktop operating system like macOS or Windows are still much easier to navigate for juggling multiple workflows. </p><p>I&#39;m able to get most of my work done (including writing this review) on the iPad Pro by displaying Google Docs and Slack in Split View and keeping my email handy in Slide Over. </p><p>However, the minute I need to dig into another app or open a different Google Doc, I find myself missing my laptop. And if you really want to use the iPad to get work done, you&#39;ll have to purchase accessories since Apple doesn&#39;t include a keyboard or Apple Pencil in the box. That means the iPad Pro can get expensive pretty quickly, considering the newest <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fproduct%2FMU8F2AM%2FA%2Fapple-pencil-2nd-generation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Apple Pencil</a> costs $129 and the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fproduct%2FMJQL3LL%2FA%2Fmagic-keyboard-for-ipad-pro-129%25E2%2580%2591inch-5th-generation-us-english-white\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Magic Keyboard</a> starts at $299.</p><p>That being said, Apple has addressed one of the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Pro</a>&#39;s biggest shortcomings compared to a traditional computer. Both the 11-inch and 12.9-inch models now support Thunderbolt, making it possible to connect the iPad to more peripherals, like high-resolution displays, USB-C hubs, and directly to dedicated cameras.</p><h2>Cameras</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3f9d51b5cea0019c45858?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple’s 2021 iPad Pro has the new M1 chip\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Apple&#39;s 2021 iPad Pro with M1 (11-inch) has a new camera feature called Center Stage\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Cameras have traditionally been overlooked in tablets, but that&#39;s not the case with the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Pro</a>. Like its predecessor, Apple&#39;s latest pro-tablet has a LiDAR sensor for measuring depth, a 12-megapixel wide camera, and a 10-megapixel ultra-wide angle camera, which could be useful for those who want to quickly shoot and edit photos and videos on the same device.</p><p>But it&#39;s the front-facing camera that&#39;s gotten a big improvement this time around. Not only does the new iPad Pro have a 12-megapixel front camera instead of a 7-megapixel camera, but it also has a new feature called Center Stage. </p><p>As the name implies, Center Stage keeps you in frame as you move during video calls, and it works in Apple&#39;s FaceTime app as well as other video conference apps. </p><p>Center Stage just works on the new <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Pro</a>, so you don&#39;t have to toggle any settings to enable it. During FaceTime calls, the camera automatically zooms in slowly to frame my face more evenly and follows me as I slide over to the left and right. It even pans out when someone else enters the scene to get them in the shot.</p><p>Some other devices like Amazon&#39;s newest Echo Show 10 and Logitech&#39;s QuickCam webcam use motors to track subjects and keep them in frame, but having it built right into the iPad makes it feel more useful and ubiquitous. </p><p>This is an example of a feature that really makes the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Pro</a> stand out in Apple&#39;s tablet lineup. It also shows how Apple can leverage the M1&#39;s power to add capabilities that weren&#39;t possible before. I only wish it came sooner, as I could imagine it being really useful for the group video calls I made to friends and family over the holidays in 2020. Hopefully this feature comes to M1 Macs at some point, too.</p><p>Otherwise, the 12-megapixel front camera on the new iPad Pro has also gotten a boost in overall quality. Take a look at the photos below, and you&#39;ll notice the iPad Pro&#39;s image looks slightly brighter and more colorful than the photo taken on the iPad Air, which has a 7-megapixel front camera.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3fa0d1b5cea0019c4585a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A selfie taken on the new 2021 iPad Pro\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A selfie taken on the new 2021 iPad Pro.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3fa44f27b4c001944519b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A selfie taken on the 2020 iPad Air\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A selfie taken on the 2020 iPad Air\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Battery life</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a3fb321b5cea0019c45861?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apple’s 2021 iPad Pro has the new M1 chip\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Apple&#39;s 2021 iPad Pro with M1 (11-inch) has a vibrant screen\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lisa Eadicicco/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Apple estimates that the new <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">iPad Pro</a> should have the same battery life as the previous-generation iPad Pro and newest <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Air</a>. Battery life is generally similar between all three tablets based on my testing, but the new 11-inch iPad Pro lasted the longest. When I played a 1080p video on YouTube with the screen set at its maximum brightness, the new 11-inch iPad Pro lasted for almost six hours. </p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-air\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Air</a>, meanwhile, died after a little more than five hours, while the older 12.9-inch iPad Pro died at the five hour mark. Remember, however, that battery life will vary depending on how you use your iPad. It&#39;s also possible that the 11-inch iPad Pro lasted longer because it&#39;s brand new, whereas the iPad Air and iPad Pro have been used previously for other tests and reviews.</p><table style=\"border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; height: 64px;\" border=\"1\"><tbody><tr style=\"height: 43px;\"><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 43px;\"> </td><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 43px;\"><strong>Apple iPad Pro (11-inch, 2021)</strong></td><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 43px;\"><strong>Apple iPad Air (2020)</strong></td><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 43px;\"><strong>Apple iPad Pro (12.9-inch 2020)</strong></td></tr><tr style=\"height: 21px;\"><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 21px;\"><strong>Battery Life</strong></td><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 21px;\">5 hours, 54 minutes</td><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 21px;\">5 hours, 17 minutes</td><td style=\"width: 25%; height: 21px;\">5 hours</td></tr></tbody></table><h2>Should you buy it?</h2><p>Yes, but only if you&#39;re looking for a tablet for editing multimedia projects and making video calls. The iPad Air can handle most of the same tasks for a cheaper price, but creatives who really want a super portable work device are likely to benefit most from the iPad Pro&#39;s M1 processor, Thunderbolt support, and advanced cameras.</p><h2>What are your alternatives?</h2><p>If you&#39;re looking to spend around $1,000 for a work device and have a more traditional workflow that involves doing a lot of research in a web browser, managing spreadsheets, and writing papers, the MacBook Air is a better choice. It still offers the long battery life and fast performance that comes with the M1 chip, but runs on Apple&#39;s desktop software that&#39;s better for multitasking.</p><p>Those who want a really nice iPad for light productivity, playing games, and watching movies should opt for the iPad Air, which has a similar design, plenty of power since it runs on the same chip as the iPhone 12, and is also compatible with the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fproduct%2FMU8F2AM%2FA%2Fapple-pencil-2nd-generation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Apple Pencil</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fproduct%2FMJQL3LL%2FA%2Fmagic-keyboard-for-ipad-pro-129%25E2%2580%2591inch-5th-generation-us-english-white\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Magic Keyboard</a>.</p><p>If you really want a tablet for traditional workflows and aren&#39;t partial to Apple, there&#39;s always Microsoft&#39;s Surface Pro 7. The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.microsoft.com%2Fen-us%2Fp%2Fsurface-pro-7%2F8N17J0M5ZZQS%2F08ZHhttps%3A%2F%2Fwww.microsoft.com%2Fen-us%2Fp%2Fsurface-pro-7%2F8N17J0M5ZZQS%2F08ZH\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Surface Pro 7</a> has a similarly compact and ultra-portable design, but runs on Windows instead of a mobile-first operating system. </p><h2>The bottom line</h2><p>The new <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-ipad%2Fipad-pro\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">iPad Pro</a> is fast, long-lasting, and has an impressive camera that keeps you in frame. But it&#39;s expensive, making it only really worth it for creative professionals that need top-notch performance and portability for working with large video and photo files in small offices or on the go. </p><p><strong>Pros</strong>: Great selfie camera that keeps you in frame, fast performance, long battery life</p><p><strong>Cons</strong>: Gets expensive quickly when you add accessories, multitasking is still better on a desktop operating system</p><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"button\" data-pid=\"6086d988a3247900115896a3\" 6-33-719_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=d_CH_04bg4s:6f5e9sXJwCw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn84@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-04-889_cb73cdf277dcb13a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/d_CH_04bg4s":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn91@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-06-595_90c4491724818aa6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436145867},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 payment by financial institutions.</p><p>Bitcoin fell as much as 26%, to $32,221.06. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/bnb-usd\">Binance Coin</a> fell 38% to $322.03, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/doge-usd\">dogecoin</a> fell 43% to 28 cents, and Ethereum&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/eth-usd\">ether</a> fell 39% to $2,094.</p><p>Virtual currencies shouldn&#39;t be used in the market as they are not supported by real value, three Chinese payment industries said on Tuesday.</p><p>Bitcoin continued its week-long slide first sparked by Elon Musk&#39;s climate-related concerns over its mining process. Billionaire Mike Novogratz predicted <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/mike-novogratz-bitcoin-outlook-elon-musk-tweets-ether-ethereum-btc-2021-5-1030439953\">bitcoin will consolidate</a> somewhere between $40,000 and $50,000 for up to six weeks after Musk&#39;s criticism of its energy use. </p><p>Tesla&#39;s cars are powered by electricity made from coal and gas, while bitcoin mining is an energy-intensive process that is said to consume more electricity annually than the <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/technology-56012952\">whole of Argentina</a>. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603929af05ddb100195f66c4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1020194172\" height=\"1997\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bitcoin mining uses vast amounts of electricity.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Olga Maltseva/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read More:</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"> </em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bank-of-america-esg-investing-sustainability-data-strategy-2021-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bank-of-america-esg-investing-sustainability-data-strategy-2021-5\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">How Bank of America is &#39;demystifying&#39; sustainable investments for its $3.5 trillion client base, according to its top ESG strategist</a></em></p><p>JPMorgan said in a note on Tuesday institutional investors seem to be shifting away from bitcoin, and moving back into traditional <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/gold-price\">gold</a>. This indicates a reversal of the trend seen over the past six months.</p><p>&#34;It is not clear what is driving this shift,&#34; strategists led by Nikolaos Panigirtzoglou wrote. &#34;Perhaps institutional investors are fleeing bitcoin as they see its previous two quarter uptrend ending and thus seek the stability of traditional gold away from the rapid downshifting of digital gold.&#34;</p><p>Separately, a blockchain research group <a href=\"https://www.elliptic.co/blog/elliptic-follows-bitcoin-ransoms-paid-by-darkside-ransomware-victims\">Elliptic found</a> the hacker group behind the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/colonial-pipeline-scheduling-system-for-nations-largest-pipeline-shut-down-2021-5\">Colonial Pipeline attack</a> received $90 million in bitcoin before it shut down last week.</p><p>That has ratcheted up regulatory risks tremendously, according to Jeffrey Halley, a senior market analyst at OANDA. &#34;China&#39;s actions raise the mercury on that front, and the Colonial situation may finally spur the US into action. I suspect they will not be alone,&#34; he said.</p><p>Halley said a drop in bitcoin to below $30,000 would not be surprising.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
