src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a51106f27b4c0019445460?format=jpeg\" alt=\"democratic debate\" height=\"2537\" width=\"5075\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Democratic presidential candidates (L-R) South Bend, Indiana Mayor Pete Buttigieg, former Vice President Joe Biden, Sen. Bernie Sanders (I-VT) and Sen. Kamala Harris (D-CA) take part in the second night of the first Democratic presidential debate on June 27, 2019 in Miami, Florida. A field of 20 Democratic presidential candidates was split into two groups of 10 for the first debate of the 2020 election, taking place over two nights at Knight Concert Hall of the Adrienne Arsht Center for the Performing Arts of Miami-Dade County, hosted by NBC News, MSNBC, and Telemundo.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Drew Angerer/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Biden was stunned when Harris attacked him during a Democratic primary debate.</li>\n<li>&#34;Well, that was some f---ing bulls---,&#34; he told Buttigieg, according to a new book.</li>\n<li>The book dives into the inside story of that primary debate night in June 2019.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Long before they became president and vice president, Joe Biden and Kamala Harris were rival Democratic candidates duking it out on the debate stage. </p><p>One of their most memorable exchanges unfolded when Harris challenged Biden, then-the frontrunner of the race, for his record on busing and race.</p><p>The scene stunned Biden, who had leaned over to tell then-Democratic candidate Pete Buttigieg, &#34;Well, that was some f---ing bulls---,&#34; according to &#34;Battle for the Soul: Inside the Democrats&#39; Campaigns to Defeat Trump,&#34; a new book by The Atlantic writer Edward-Isaac Dovere.</p><p>In an <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/magazine/2021/05/19/edward-isaac-dovere-2020-campaign-book-excerpt-joe-biden-kamala-harris-489347\">excerpt of the book</a> published by Politico, Dovere dove into the inside story of that tense primary debate night that took place in June 2019.</p><p>Shortly before the debate, Biden had come under fire for boasting about his reputation of working across the aisle. During a fundraiser in New York City, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-democrats-joe-bidens-record-before-debates-2019-6\">he spoke about his career as a senator</a> and referenced legislating alongside pro-segregationist lawmakers.</p><p>&#34;Well guess what? At least there was some civility. We got things done. We didn&#39;t agree on much of anything. We got things done,&#34; Biden had said.</p><p>Harris had been readying an attack on Biden over his comments, and her team had compiled opposition research to hit him hard on racial issues, according to Dovere. Once the topic was brought up on stage, Harris&#39; aides advised her to go for the jugular. </p><p>&#34;I do not believe you are a racist, and I agree with you when you commit yourself to the importance of finding common ground,&#34; she told Biden on stage. &#34;But I also believe, and it&#39;s personal - it was hurtful to hear you talk about the reputations of two United States senators who built their reputations and career on the segregation of race in this country.&#34;</p><p>&#34;And it was not only that, but you also worked with them to oppose busing,&#34; Harris continued. &#34;And, you know, there was a little girl in California who was part of the second class to integrate her public schools, and she was bused to school every day. And that little girl was me.&#34;</p><p>Biden sought to defend himself and said Harris&#39; comments were a mischaracterization. When the debate cut to commercial, Dovere reported that Biden offered his candid reaction of the scene to Buttigieg, whom he then hardly knew. Buttigieg now serves as Biden&#39;s transportation secretary. </p><p>The moment now appears to be a blip in Biden and Harris&#39; relationship. Harris dropped out of the race in December 2019 and Biden announced her as his vice presidential pick in August of last year. At the time, they <a href=\"https://www.realclearpolitics.com/video/2020/08/17/kamala_harris_dismisses_past_biden_criticism_it_was_a_debate.html\">attempted</a> to downplay the combative exchange.</p><p>&#34;It was a debate,&#34; Harris said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 19 May 2021 14:37:27 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/60a52221f27b4c00194454e6?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"ab5ca420bd585fb4db22901ea776fd1a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn7@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-00-733_1d090f67a761762e.webp","destWidth":1874,"destHeight":1405,"sourceBytes":98934,"destBytes":98934,"author":"tlevin@businessinsider.com (Tim Levin)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/609963ccba78eb001906e2f9?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn4@2020_5/2021/05/19/14-56-06-183_9235a4065e09a365.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn88@2020_2/2021/05/19/14-56-05-974_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=IF_MM9yBftU:fbe8w7sg0Bs:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn36@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-03-597_55b481553a419a10.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=IF_MM9yBftU:fbe8w7sg0Bs:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_6/2021/05/19/14-56-02-340_fa6432381d3e78e9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn71@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-33-719_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=IF_MM9yBftU:fbe8w7sg0Bs:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn24@2020_4/2021/05/19/14-56-01-858_37f3b70274e59069.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/IF_MM9yBftU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn80@2020_3/2021/05/19/14-56-05-287_1addf7467e6c4a8c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1621436145873},{"createdTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","updatedTime":"2021-05-19 22:55:45","title":"How the 28-year-old CEO of a sports company backed by Adidas' venture fund spends her day","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trisha-goyal-tennis-one-of-sports-youngest-ceos-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1b2fef27b4c0019444bf8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Break the Love Trisha Goyal\" height=\"673\" width=\"897\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goyal cofounded Break the Love with Tess Szymanski.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Break the Love / Gabby Perez</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Trisha Goyal is the CEO and cofounder of <a href=\"https://www.breakthelove.com/\">Break the Love</a>, an app that allows people to book tennis classes and enter tournaments. </li>\n<li>She spends a lot of her day assessing design with her team and her customers.</li>\n<li>To Insider, she breaks down how she spends a typical day. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>It all began with a Google search in 2017. </p><p>Trisha Goyal was in Connecticut looking for a place to play tennis, and quickly realized her task wasn&#39;t so simple. </p><p>Most of her options were either too expensive or not flexible enough to fit with her schedule. In 2019, she co-created <a href=\"https://breakthelove.com\">Break the Love</a>, a digital platform that allows people to book tennis lessons, enter tournaments, and meet other players. </p><p>Tennis has a stigma attached to it: It&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.tennis365.com/tennis-features/exclusive-judy-murray-urges-tennis-to-shed-its-elitist-tag-and-open-its-doors-to-the-masses/\">exclusive</a> and <a href=\"https://tennispredict.com/why-is-tennis-so-expensive/\">expensive</a>, said Goyal, who&#39;s now 28, lives in New York City, and has been playing the sport since she was eight years old. That&#39;s why she wanted to build inclusivity into the company&#39;s ethos.</p><p>Break the Love started by partnering with nonprofits around New York City but has now entered into revenue partnerships with the United States Tennis Association and Wilson Sporting Goods. Spread across 10 cities in places such as New York and California, Break the Love hosts its own classes, is creating its own tennis tournaments, and has 5,000 active users. </p><p>The company saw record growth amid the pandemic as people sought to go outside during times of isolation and there are 20,000 on the waitlist for the locations in which Break the Love has yet to launch. Declining to share exact revenue, Goyal says the company won the Adidas&#39; Reimagine Sports Grant through the iFundWomen&#39;s grant program and was accepted into the Adidas-backed incubator program <a href=\"https://www.leadsports.com/\">leAD</a>. </p><p>To Insider, Goyal breaks down what a typical day looks like, from taking partnership calls all morning, to tennis classes late in the evening. </p><h2>She wakes up at 7:30 a.m. </h2><p>After making a cup of coffee and walking her dog for 20 minutes, Goyal opens Instagram to post the scheduled morning marketing for <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/breakthelove/?hl=en\">Break the Love,</a> highlighting upcoming classes and other events. </p><p>Around 8 a.m. Goyal takes a shower, grabs another cup of coffee, and begins going through her emails. &#34;I usually scan through all of my emails and list down which emails are the highest priority that I need to respond to in the morning versus the afternoon,&#34; she said.</p><h2>Her first-morning meeting is around 9 a.m. </h2><p>Goyal stops checking emails around 9 a.m. and begins meetings. There are only about four full-time employees at the company, and her first meeting is usually with her engineering team, as Break the Love is both an app and website. They spend an hour testing new features.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1b118f27b4c0019444bed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Break the love Trisha Goyal\" height=\"3992\" width=\"2994\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goyal and her team have been making flyers for Break the Love to market the company.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Break the Love</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Break the Love already offers classes for beginners and advanced players, and charges users a fee to attend classes and tournaments. Classes start as low as $39. The platform also trains athletes who, afterward, can serve as instructors for the classes.</p><p>Goyal says Break the Love builds all the tools it needs in-house, and it&#39;s something to which they must pay close attention. There is a big difference, for example, between launching a new tennis product in New York versus Florida, Goyal says, and the team must know how to have a product be effective in both markets. </p><p>In New York, for example, the problem is typically where to find courts and where people can learn about tennis without spending too much money (private lessons can cost an average of $125 an hour, she said.) In places like Florida, however, it mainly comes down to finding people to play with, and places to learn the sport that are comfortable and inclusive for everybody. </p><p>On this day, the company released a map view so people can pinpoint the exact location of tennis courts before deciding to join a class or enter into a tournament. &#34;After we feel good about what we are about to push out, we spend the second half of our hour doing discovery around new features,&#34; Goyal added. The team then spent thirty minutes mapping out features that could better predict weather patterns. </p><h2>After morning meetings, she connects with investors </h2><p>Goyal spends about thirty minutes reviewing scheduled programs for the week, then goes back to her inbox and starts answering emails from investors. </p><p>She gets another cup of coffee, and around 11:30 a.m., she takes a quick break to get fresh air and lunch. While eating, she starts working on a creative partnership deck as well as more proposals. &#34;For us, partnerships are a big part of how we grow our number of courts we have access to,&#34; she said, citing, for example, how the company works with various Parks and Recreation Departments throughout the nation. </p><p>Aside from partnering with both public and private tennis courts, Break the Love provides tennis rentals for beginners.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1b109f27b4c0019444bea?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Break the love Trisha Goyal\" height=\"519\" width=\"790\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Break the Love / Gabby Perez</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Around  2 p.m. she has more calls</h2><p>Goyal grabs another cup of coffee then hops on another call. On this day, she spoke to Wilson Sporting Goods to plan a new series launching this summer called &#34;Access Courts,&#34; which seeks to help get more people into tennis. </p><p>Since she&#39;s often on back-to-back phone calls, Goyal likes to schedule &#34;walking calls&#34; outdoors. Afterward, she squeezes in calls with some customers to receive feedback on programs. Gen Zers and millennials are outspoken in what they like and don&#39;t like these days, she said, predicting more will start demanding inclusive and convenient tennis access. The goal is for her company to be at the forefront of that push, the same way <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cami-tellez-cofounder-wants-to-build-a-billion-dollar-brand-2020-10\">Parade</a> makes inclusive underwear or FENTY Beauty makes inclusive skin foundations. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1b2adf27b4c0019444bf5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Break the love Trisha Goyal\" height=\"755\" width=\"1007\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goyal on her way to a practice.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Break the Love</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;What you see on pro-circuit tennis doesn&#39;t trickle down fully to the club system which is where tennis predominantly lives and is predominantly run by the same kind of people that can make the sport feel intimidating,&#34; she said. &#34;Just like golf.&#34; </p><p>After the calls, she looks at ways to modify existing program formats based on the customer feedback. </p><h2>Around 6 p.m. she tries out her classes </h2><p>She spends time sending personalized welcome emails, then changes into her tennis clothes to join one of Break the Love&#39;s tennis classes.  &#34;This is one of my favorite parts of my day because really our product is the on-court experience so it is always really rewarding to experience it myself,&#34; she said. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a1b119f27b4c0019444bee?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Break the love Trisha Goyal\" height=\"2676\" width=\"4014\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Break the Love / Jenna Fernandez</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>At around 8:30 p.m., she finally makes it back home </h2><p>Goyal showers and makes dinner. She tries not to check her emails but, instead finds herself designing new marketing material. Before bed, she walks her dog again. Around 10:30 p.m., she falls asleep, so she can wake up tomorrow and do it all over again.  </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a4ed73e25d05001880c655?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1299369052\" height=\"2250\" width=\"4500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Critics have long highlighted bitcoin&#39;s US regulators, which could step up enforcement.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><strong><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestrkets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Recent high-profile cyber attacks in which hackers demanded to be paid in cryptocurrencies have turned an uncomfortable spotlight on digital tokens and their use in crime.</p><p>One analyst said the ransomware attack on the Colonial Pipeline was facilitated by cryptocurrencies, which &#34;will not go unnoticed by the US government and other countries.&#34;</p><p>Hackers severely <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/colonial-largest-us-fuel-pipeline-operator-shuts-down-operations-after-cyberattack-2021-5\">disrupted the US energy network</a> earlier in May when they attacked the crucial Colonial Pipeline&#39;s computing systems. To get the system back up and running, Colonial paid a ransom of nearly $5 million in cryptocurrency, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-05-13/colonial-pipeline-paid-hackers-nearly-5-million-in-ransom\">Bloomberg reported</a>, citing people familiar with the matter.</p><p>Days later, hackers targeted Ireland&#39;s health service and also demanded a ransom <a href=\"https://www.irishtimes.com/news/health/bitcoin-ransom-will-not-be-paid-following-cyber-attack-on-hse-computer-systems-1.4564957\">be paid in bitcoin</a>.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd\">Bitcoin</a> has crashed in recent days after Elon Musk said Tesla would no longer accept the token as payment, due to its &#34;insane&#34; and environmentally damaging energy use. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-cryptocurrencies-china-crypto-crackdown-price-outlook-2021-5-1030445035\">Cryptocurrencies slid again</a> on Tuesday after Chinese regulators cracked down on the use of digital assets for payments.</p><p>But Jeffrey Halley, senior market analyst at currency firm Oanda, said the so-called ransomware attacks had been an underappreciated factor.</p><p>&#34;With Elon Musk grabbing all the headlines on his bitcoin/dogecoin pivot, the real issue is the $5 million ransom paid by Colonial Pipeline,&#34; he said.</p><p>&#34;Attacks on critical US infrastructure facilitated by cryptocurrencies will not go unnoticed by the US government and other countries. I would argue that the regulatory threat to cryptocurrencies has increased exponentially.&#34;</p><p>Critics of bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies have long argued that they facilitate crime thanks to their anonymous and decentralized nature, which means they are very hard to trace and link to individuals.</p><p>Treasury Secretary Janet Yellen <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bitcoin-price-cryptocurrency-should-be-curtailed-terrorism-concerns-yellen-2021-1\">said in January</a> that she was concerned about cryptocurrencies for this reason. &#34;I think many are used - at least in a transaction sense - mainly for illicit financing,&#34; she told lawmakers during her confirmation hearing.</p><p>Gary Gensler, the Chair of the Securities and Exchange Commission markets regulator, has made similar criticisms in the past.</p><p>&#34;Beyond use on the darknet, there are those around the globe who seek to use these new technologies to thwart government oversight of money laundering, tax evasion, terrorism financing, or evading sanctions regimes,&#34; he <a href=\"https://www.congress.gov/115/meeting/house/108562/witnesses/HHRG-115-AG00-Wstate-GenslerG-20180718.pdf\">told Congress</a> in 2018.</p><p>Although cryptocurrency companies that deal with customers in the US are covered by various financial regulations, the digital asset markets is largely a grey area outside the traditional world of finance. Regulators have consistently warned that investors should only buy in if they&#39;re <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/cryptocurrencies-bitcoin-dogecoin-risks-lose-money-bank-of-england-andrew-bailey-1030396958\">willing to lose all their money</a>.</p><p>In the US, regulators are keeping a close eye on cryptocurrencies but have not yet committed to any major rule changes during the latest digital asset boom.</p><p>Fox Business reported in April that Gensler is <a href=\"https://video.foxbusiness.com/v/6249208738001#sp=show-clips\">waiting for the Treasury</a> to review the currency cryptocurrency rules before the SEC lays out its approach. Fox said Gensler is likely to step up enforcement action.</p><p>Regulators are likely to increase their focus on crypto as ransomware attacks become more prevalent, said Rahul Bhushan, co-founder of Rize ETF, which runs a cybersecurity fund.</p><p>Yet Bhushan said a stronger &#34;regulatory framework around cryptocurrencies… will help legitimize that market.&#34;</p><p>Michael Shaulov, chief executive of crypto firm Fireblocks, said: &#34;The true solution is a capability for law enforcement agencies around the world to distribute real-time information about illicit activities allowing wallet and custody providers to block these funds in transit.&#34;</p><p>Colonial Pipeline has been contacted for comment.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a t?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingests&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>Odds of a potential &#34;melt-up&#34; in the stock market are rising as institutional investors raise near record levels of cash, <a href=\"https://fsinsight.com/\">Fundstrat&#39;s</a> Tom Lee said in a note on Tuesday.</p><p>Since the start of 2021, money market balances of institutional investors have surged by $297 billion to more than $3 trillion, nearly matching the peak levels seen during the height of the COVID-19 pandemic in May of 2020. </p><p>The near-record cash raise by professional investors comes even as the stock market managed to move higher so far this year, with the S&#38;P 500 up 11%, and as data continues to show improving momentum for the US economy.</p><p>&#34;Institutional investors have been steady sellers of risk assets even as equities managed to post gains,&#34; Lee said.</p><p>While professional investors have been raising cash, the money market balances of retail investors has fallen by $76 billion in 2021 to about $1.5 trillion, according to the note. Assuming that $76 billion in retail money flowed into the stock market, it has been more than offset by the cash raise of institutions.</p><p>To Lee, the current dynamic is a sign of capitulation among institutional investors, which could potentially lead to a &#34;melt-up&#34; in the stock market as they look to deploy the cash raised back into the stock market.</p><p>The cash raised by institutions coincides with survey data from the National Association of Active Investment Managers that showed positioning in the S&#38;P 500 is the most cautious since April 2020.</p><p>&#34;Anytime investors are this cautious, it is a strong &#39;contrarian&#39; buy signal. Thus, we see high odds of a market melt-up,&#34; Lee said.</p><p>Lee recommended investors take advantage of this dislocation by buying cyclical stocks poised to benefit from a full reopening of the US economy, including stocks in the energy, materials, and financials sectors, according to the note. Lee is cautious on technology stocks and said investors should use any strength to reduce exposure to the sector. </p><figure>\n\t<img
